Japan Considers Countermeasures for the Anglo-Indian-Japanese Trade Conference 25

Regarding the British Proposals as Unfavorable to Itself

(Tokyo) With the Anglo-Japanese and Indo-Japanese conferences about to open, the Japanese Foreign Ministry and other ministries and related people from the private sector have repeatedly held meetings to consider countermeasures. However, because the true intentions of the British and Indian sides are unknown, the Foreign Ministry has issued new basic instructions to the Japanese representatives and will determine the detailed policy depending on the situation of the conference. The general outline of the Japanese countermeasures currently being formulated by the Foreign Ministry is as follows: a joint meeting will be held on the seventeenth to make a final decision. (1) The Indo-Japanese Simla Conference will discuss the sudden problems between the Indian and Japanese representatives, with the content reached being the final conclusion. (2) The Simla Conference will formulate a new treaty due to the expiration of the current Indo-Japanese trade treaty on October 10, with reciprocity as its aim, that is, to prevent the initiation of the Indian Business Protection Act with the new treaty. (3) The main topic of the conference will be cotton textiles. (4) Both Britain and India are excluding Japanese goods. Japan demands its reduction, and at the same time, Japan also expresses its sincerity in increasing purchases of Indian cotton, oil, hides, and other goods. (Fourteenth Japan United News Telegram)

(Tokyo) The British government's reply regarding the Anglo-Japanese-Indian private sector consultative conference to be held in London and Simla was sent to the Foreign Ministry by Ambassador Matsudaira today. The content is as follows: (1) The scope of the consultation includes markets in third countries other than Britain and Japan. (2) The items for consultation are not limited to cotton yarn and cloth, but also include rayon and blended fabrics. (3) The nature of the agreement is not clearly stated, and it seems to be attempting to set up a market agreement for distributing markets. The above three points are not consistent with the main interests and claims of Japanese businesses, and Japan's fundamental claims are: (1) An agreement on the markets of third countries is meaningless because it only concerns the interests of operators in third countries. (2) If competitors in the rayon industry, such as German and Italian rayon manufacturers, are not included, and only an Anglo-Japanese-Indian rayon agreement is concluded, it will be harmful and useless to the Japanese rayon industry. (3) The agreement is limited to the quantity of goods exported to British India and other territories by Britain, India, and Japan, but it opposes non-enforceable market distribution agreements and price agreements. Therefore, Japan is in a position where it cannot but oppose the British proposal, so it will immediately seek the opinions of businesses and become familiar with them. (Fourteenth Den-tsu Telegram)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Foreign Ministry plans to submit a list of representatives for the Simla Conference to the cabinet meeting tomorrow, seeking government approval. Tomorrow, Sawada, Morio, and Miyake will be officially appointed as Japanese representatives to India. The content of their instructions will be decided at a joint official-private consultation meeting on August 17, and then handed over to the three representatives. Current Commentary

Internal Water Worries and External Troubles 33

Fact

China has historically managed water. There are also so-called internal worries and external troubles. The emergency protection against hazards on the sea dikes is external, while the management of the Yangtze and Yellow Rivers is internal. If these internal and external water worries are not addressed with full force and a fundamental, large-scale treatment to eliminate the source of their disasters, then we will suffer every year, greatly affecting the national economy and the people's livelihood. Recently, there have been reports of urgent crises on the sea dikes in Baoshan and Chongming in Jiangsu Province. After Supervisory Yuan Commissioner Gao Yihan personally inspected the dike construction and witnessed its dangers, he made a special report to the central government. The main points included requesting the central government to allocate funds for emergency repairs, and requesting that a certain tonnage be allocated from the US cotton and wheat loan specifically for river and dike stone works. Furthermore, he ordered the Jiangsu Department of Finance to allocate the dike construction funds listed in the budgets after the 18th year of the Republic in full to prepare for the construction of dikes and embankments. If the country truly wants to defend against sea disasters and manage sea dikes, it must do so as Commissioner Gao said. Only with sufficient funds can we take action. However, at a time when the central government's finances are extremely tight, relying solely on the government's borrowing and allocation to accomplish a major task may be hopeless. Under these circumstances, if the sea dikes do not plan for remedies, the consequences will be disastrous once something happens. The people of Jiangsu Province, in order to protect their lives and property, can only quickly rise up to seek self-defense and exert all their efforts to assist the central government and share this huge responsibility with the government. This is the most important thing to pay attention to in defending against external threats.

As for the so-called major internal worry, the water level of the Yangtze River recently also warned of danger, causing fear among the people, as if the great disaster of the previous year would happen again. Fortunately, the water volume upstream naturally decreased, and it did not become a major disaster. Unexpectedly, the water level of the Yangtze River had just receded, and the water level of the Yellow River suddenly rose sharply. The rapid currents in Luoyang surged, and the northern section of the Pinghan Railway Yellow River Iron Bridge was scoured by the rapid currents. The bridge pier tilted eastward. According to the Railway Bureau, the slope has already tilted eastward by two centimeters, and the situation is already very dangerous. Even if the water level does not increase further, it is feared that it will not be able to be repaired within three to five days. The railway traffic between Pinghan has been greatly affected, not to mention the flooding of residents' fields and the destruction of houses along the river, the losses are incalculable. What we should pay attention to is Caozhou and eight counties in western Shandong besides Zhengzhou and Kaifeng. Several breaches have already occurred there, with water heads reaching a height of more than one zhang and coming with great ferocity. If the water does not flow through Hebei Province but enters Shandong from Caozhou, Shandong may be spared from the disaster. However, if it follows the old course and breaches the dikes between Kaifeng and Lanfeng and goes straight to Huaihai, then the people of eastern Henan will inevitably be buried in the pools of water, and the areas of Xuzhou and Haizhou will also be reduced to swamps. Northern Jiangsu, from Tongshan and Suining to Qingjiangpu, will all be subjected to the disaster. Furthermore, the people of the counties east of Tianjin have suffered greatly in the anti-Japanese war and are still recovering from their numerous wounds. Who would have thought that near Yutian, trenches crisscrossed and mountain torrents suddenly broke out, flooding more than 3,000 hectares of fertile land and submerging more than 200 villages? Baochi and Fengrun were also affected to a lesser extent. The upstream of the Yongding River also simultaneously experienced floods, with Xuanhua and Huailai being the most severe. This is something we cannot bear to describe in detail.

The danger of internal and external water disasters in China is like this. However, these water disasters did not start recently. Throughout history, government officials and people have studied water management plans. The books on this can be said to be abundant, but in the end, they are limited by talent and financial resources, or limited by busy personnel, and they have never considered this century-long plan. Once a disaster suddenly occurs, the so-called good officials can only temporarily work hard and desperately on emergency rescue and protection work. Fortunately, if it is effective, it will only be able to cope with temporary disasters. One of the most important words from water management experts of the past is: "Discharge is more important than defense." Whether it is managing the sea, the river, or the river, we must abandon the old method of building dams and blocking water, and start with guiding and dredging to make the water flow smoothly downstream. Only then can we avoid temporary busyness and lay the foundation for a century-long plan. In recent years, natural science has developed, and river and sea engineering has made amazing progress. If we all truly want to fundamentally manage and eliminate this continuous huge disaster, it may not be impossible. It depends on the determination of the Chinese people.

Central National Government Two Memorial Week Reports 34

Gu Zhenggan ···· Party and Political Power

Yu Youren ···· Rural Revival

(Nanjing) The Central Party Headquarters held a memorial week at 8:00 a.m. on the 14th. Present were Central Committee members Ye Chucang, Ju Zheng, Chen Lifu, Chu Minyi, Gu Zhenggan, Li Ciwen, and central staff members, totaling about 600 people. Chairman Ye Chucang led the ceremony. Gu Zhenggan reported, stating in brief that in recent years, there have been loud calls for the opening of political power by the party. Party comrades hold different attitudes on how the party should approach political power, either advocating for openness and an early end to the period of political tutelage, or advocating for temporarily not opening up political power according to certain steps of political tutelage and constitutionalism. The reason is to prevent the reactionary faction from seizing political power and repeating the mistakes of the Xinhai Revolution. The starting point is out of love for the party and the country. However, in his personal opinion, he advocates for ending the period of political tutelage and opening up political power as soon as possible. Since the party came to power, it has coincided with domestic and foreign troubles in the country. All political responsibilities are attributed to the party, and the relationship between the party and the people has become that of ruler and ruled. At this time, based on party ideology and objective facts, it is necessary to establish a new policy. It is not necessary to rigidly adhere to the division of the period of absolute political tutelage and constitutionalism. Convening the National Assembly in advance is also a factual need, and opening up political power should not be interpreted as abandoning political power. Any political party that does not want to seize political power and maintain political power certainly does not want to abandon political power. The party is no different. Therefore, the issue is not whether to open up political power, but the party's ability and whether it has the support of the people. Now we should strive to enrich the party's strength and consolidate the party's foundation. Then, after opening up political power, the political power should still belong to the party. Also, when opening up political power, it should not be handed over to the reactionary faction, but to the revolutionary people. As for fearing that the reactionary faction will seize political power, there is no need to worry about it. (Central News Agency, 14th)

(Nanjing) The National Government held a memorial week at 9:00 a.m. on the 14th. Present were Yu Youren, Lin Xiang, Chen Shaokuan, He Yaozu, Huang Musong, Chu Minyi, Lü Chao, and National Government staff members, totaling about 400 people. Chairman Lin led the ceremony. Yu Youren reported, stating in brief that he often went outside Zhongshan Gate and saw many melon growers planting many melons, and the melons produced were also excellent, but the selling price was very low. Melon eaters were happy, but melon sellers were very bitter. Although this principle is not understood by farmers, it is actually a sign of rural bankruptcy. In recent years, our country has encountered domestic and foreign troubles, natural and man-made disasters. After the September 18th Incident, it was followed by the January 28th Incident. Recently, the war in Lai and North China has just ended, and then there were the troubles in Sichuan. The great flood of the 20th year has not yet recovered. This year, the Yellow River has also affected several provinces. The suffering of the people is deepening day by day. The sound of rural bankruptcy has spread throughout the country. The severity of the national crisis should not exceed today. Our country is founded on agriculture, and the foundation of the country is placed on hardworking farmers. The harvest of hardworking farmers is not enough to make a living, or even displaced and unable to live. People's livelihood is exhausted, endangering the foundation of the country, and the pain is deepening. As the saying goes, "Think of the pain after it is over," but just thinking about the pain does not help. We should think and do after the pain is over. We should consider how to do it to restore the pain. In addition, we should have a comprehensive plan for the rural revival plan and seek overall facilities. The government is not unwilling to seek relief, but only piecemeal, resulting in twice the effort and half the result. In the future, I hope that the government and the people of the whole country will do their best to restore the rural plan. The national crisis will eventually be eliminated. (Central News Agency, 14th)

After the ceremony, a proclamation was issued to the people, declaring that the protection of the people's rights in the Constitution will be fully restored, freedom of speech will be guaranteed for newspapers, economic conditions will be improved, taxes will be reduced, government expenditures will be strictly economized, and life and property will be safe, advising the people to settle down and resume their businesses.

The new president today discussed the formation of a cabinet with leaders of various parties and important labor unions. It is expected that a mixed cabinet will be formed, and labor will also have representatives in it.

Cuban political leaders did not show significant resentment when they heard the news that the United States had sent warships. Unresolved Concerns in Southern Ireland 64

Blue Shirts Hold Periodic Memorial for Martyrs

Valera Actively Prevents Disturbances

Reuters, Berlin, 13th - General O'Duffy's National Executive Committee of the National Guard held its first meeting today to discuss the issue of commemorating revolutionary martyrs on August 20th. A unanimous decision was made to proceed as planned. This issue was raised by General O'Duffy, who advocated holding memorial services in churches across the country next Sunday. O'Duffy originally proposed a large parade of Blue Shirts today, but it was prevented by Valera, so the memorial service was rescheduled to be held in churches next Sunday. Last night, some young people gathered outside the National Guard headquarters and suddenly attacked the Blue Shirts as they came out, leading to clashes. However, the troublemakers were quickly dispersed by the police.

National, Dublin, 13th - Today, Sunday, has passed peacefully without any incidents. However, the tension of the situation has not lessened to this day. Police in various places are constantly patrolling fully armed. Armored vehicles are stationed at important locations in various cities. Soldiers in various military camps are also in full readiness. Furthermore, because the Blue Shirts declared that the destination of their march was the Irish Revolutionary Martyrs Memorial in front of the Parliament, Valera's old troops, armed with live ammunition and tear gas, were stationed around the memorial to defend it. Only about 300 people were allowed to pass through the area to lay wreaths at the memorial throughout the day. The families of revolutionary martyrs such as Griffith and Collins did not attend, even though they had received passes in advance. Former President Cosgrave, General O'Duffy, and other anti-government figures also did not appear. The current government has organized a wartime council, presided over by five senior military officers, specifically to deal with the issue of citizens privately possessing firearms. From this, it can be seen that the government is actively trying to prevent future disturbances.

Reuters, Dublin, 14th - Although Valera has banned the Blue Shirts from marching in formation, General O'Duffy has begun recruiting new members on a large scale. O'Duffy has sent officers to major cities in the Free State to increase the momentum of the Blue Shirt movement. According to the National Guard headquarters in Dublin today, the Blue Shirts currently have 40,000 members and are expected to double in number within a week so that they can march in formation across Southern Ireland on the 20th of this month.

Brüning Tired of Political Life 65

National, Berlin, 13th - According to recent reports, former German Chancellor Brüning will soon enter a monastery to live in seclusion and continue his scientific research. Brüning currently holds a seat in the Reichstag, but it is feared that he will resign from that position as well. Brüning is currently 48 years old and has studied history, philosophy, and political science. Before the European War, he obtained a doctorate in economics. From 1914 to 1918, he served in the Western Front as a machine gun squad leader. He was injured in the Battle of the Marne and, after recovering, engaged in labor relief work. In 1924, he was elected to the Reichstag. In 1930, President Hindenburg appointed him as Chancellor, which was the peak of Brüning's career. Last year, Brüning was overthrown by his political enemy, the current Chancellor Hitler, but Hitler unanimously praised Brüning's integrity and dedication to his duties. Furthermore, German newspapers have always referred to Brüning as the "Monk Chancellor." Now that it has become a reality, it is also a good story.

The breach at Changyuan, the Floodwater Approaching the Shandong Province 79

=Another Break in Changyuan on the 11th=

=The Crest of Floodwater Heading towards Dongming and Heze=

=Heading towards the Grand Canal, Flooding Directly into the Yangtze River=

A dispatch from Jinan reports that the Yellow River's floods this year are very different from those of the past. Before August 5th, the water level rose steadily, reaching 30.32 meters at Luokou, the highest water level in Shandong Province this year, exceeding last year's water level by more than two inches. From the 5th to the 8th or 9th, the river water suddenly dropped sharply, a troubling sign. Fortunately, Shandong Province has been actively managing the river works for years, and the dikes are considered solid, which brought some reassurance to the people. Unexpectedly, during this period, a warning was received that several breaches had been dug in the people's dikes in Changyuan County, Hebei Province, by bandits, and the water was tending to flood towards Shandong Province. Han Fuqu, the Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, regularly dispatched Zhang Lianjia, the Director of the River Affairs Bureau, to inspect the Linshengtun area upstream. Zhang set off after receiving the order. On the 10th, Zhang returned from his inspection, saying that the flood (the water discharged from Changyuan) was not large, and there were still more than ninety li from the northern bank of the dike in Puyang County, Shandong Province. All works in our province are extremely solid, and there is no cause for concern. Unexpectedly, the River Affairs Bureau today (12th) connected to the upstream general section chief Chen Wenmo's telegram from the two days, claiming that the No. 2 Fen Village of the first section on the southern bank of the Yellow River in Hebei Province broke at 12:00 noon that morning, and Dongming County in Hebei Province and Heze County in western Shandong Province will be the first to suffer. A special person was sent to Fen Village to check the water situation, and it was reported that the water crest in the river was more than one zhang high, and it was still seven or eight chi from the Shandong border. Wen Ri's telegram also said that he had inquired to Lin Danzhen, the head of the fourth section of Hebei Province, who said that the river water rose sharply by six or seven small chi at one o'clock in the afternoon, and the Stone Village Pass on the north bank (which was previously excavated by bandits in Changyuan County, in the north of the river) was being blocked. After this water discharge, work had been stopped. Above this pass, there were four other breaches, the largest of which was more than five li wide. The main stream was rushing and extremely turbulent, and the disaster in Changyuan Puyang and other counties in Hebei Province was extremely serious. At the same time, the Fen Village Pang Village area of the first duan on the south bank was also inundated into a mouth, overflowing outside the embankment. At first, it was only a few zhang wide, but later it became larger and larger. At this moment, it has reached more than fifty zhang, and the water is also fierce. The water head has passed Dongming County, and the Caozhu area in western Shandong Province will all become marshes. According to this, the River Affairs Bureau is preparing for prevention, and then received a telegram from Sun Zerang, the magistrate of Heze County, saying that the north bank of the Yellow River in Changyuan County had broken several more mouths on the You day, and the mouth was several miles wide. At the same time, the south bank also broke a mouth of more than thirty zhang. At 12:00 that night, the water head had passed Dongming, and this afternoon (12th), it can flow to Heze, etc.

Upon investigation, the reasons for the Yellow River's breach this time and the subsequent flooding of Shandong Province are as follows: In the upstream area of Shaanzhou, there was continuous rain, and mountain floods broke out. The river water flowed downwards with the high and low water levels, like a galloping horse. The downstream river channel is narrow and has many bends. The riverbed is higher than the flat ground. The river water comes downstream and is restricted by the bends, so its force is fierce and powerful. In addition, the dikes along the river in the downstream provinces always consider the economic strength of each province and the experience of the river affairs personnel to determine the safety of one area, so the situation is different and the dike quality is different. Moreover, due to years of civil war and foreign aggression, the authorities have never had a unified plan, and even if there is a plan, it has not been implemented throughout the entire river. Only the provinces are governing themselves, mostly using the old method of ○blocking, treating the head when it hurts, and treating the feet when it hurts. This great disaster has been expected by most people for a long time. As for the reason for affecting Shandong Province, it is because Heze is adjacent to Dongming and Changyuan in Hebei, and Fan County, Yucheng, Shouzhang, Yanggu, Puyang, Dongping, and other counties in western Shandong are just within the people's embankment set of Hebei and Shandong provinces, so the Yellow River's breach in Changyuan, Hebei, first flooded the counties in western Shandong. Now the water crest has arrived in Heze, and soon the counties east of Heze will be a vast ocean and become a marsh.

According to a group of experts, this water crest flows to the Fen Shui Long Wu Temple in Dongping County. If it turns to the north, it will flow into the low-lying areas of Linqing and Wucheng, enter the North Canal, and still be discharged into the river channel, causing less harm. If it turns to the south, it will enter the South Canal, pass through the Nanyang and Weishan lakes, and flood directly into the Yangtze River, then the disaster area will expand, and the losses will be difficult to estimate. However, judging from the current trend of the water crest, it is mostly to the south. It is reported that the River Affairs Bureau believes that the Yellow River has already become a disaster, and in addition to reporting to the Provincial Government, it has also sent separate telegrams to the counties to strictly prevent and block it, so as to avoid general flooding. Today (12th), the Yellow River's water levels in Shandong Province vary, with some rising and some falling, and it has eased slightly. (12th)

The Lineup of the Southern Route Bandit Suppression Army 80

│Will Use Surprise Troops to Copy Bandit Rear Areas│

A dispatch from Shantou reports that after the Southern Route Army Headquarters moved to the Dayu Ridge, it immediately began a large-scale bandit suppression operation according to the original plan. The deployment of its forces is roughly as follows: In the Ganzhou area, there are the Li Zhenqiu, Ye Zhao, and Chen Zhangfu divisions of the First Column under Yu Hanmou, with a defense line from Ganzhou to Nanxiong and Xinfeng. From Nanxiong to Sannan, Lianping, Heping, and Longchuan, there are the Wang Zanbin, Zhang Meixin, and Li Hanhun divisions of the Third Column. This route is to protect the upper reaches of the northeastern rivers of Guangdong Province, and it was originally designated as the most important line of operations. From Anyuan, Xunwu, Xingning, Pingyuan, Jiaoling to Wuping and Shanghang, there are the Huang Renhuan, Huang Yanzhen, and Huang Zhiwen divisions of the Second Column. This line is a fortress to protect the border between Fujian, Guangdong, and Jiangxi. If we consider the bandits currently concentrated in Huichang Junmenling, this line can be called the front line in the confrontation. From Yongding, Longyan, Liancheng to Changting, there are the Qu Shounian, Shen Guanghan, and Zhang Yan divisions of the Fourth Column of the 19th Route Army. This line can be called the attacking line of the National Army, because Changting is very close to Ruijin, the Red Capital. If Changting is recovered, it can immediately attack the rear of the pseudo-Central District of Ruijin and Huichang, mutually responding to the defense line of Ganzhou. However, the bandits' tactics are to specialize in the deep mountains on the border of Fujian and Jiangxi, using the dangerous areas of mountains and rivers, attacking the bandit suppression army on one side and holding on to Junmenling on the other. Then, they send a large force into Qingliu and Yong'an in northern Fujian, attempting to disrupt the pre-determined formation of the bandit suppression army. Therefore, in the past half month, the front lines on both sides have changed repeatedly. However, the bandit suppression army has realized that the bandits are trying to invade Fujian, so it has also deployed surprise troops to copy the bandit rear areas. (August 8th)

=Henan and Anhui Troops Jointly Suppressing on a Large Scale=

=The Bandits in Huoqiu Are Again Trying to Stir Up Trouble=

A dispatch from Bengbu reports that the defeated soldiers who fled from Henan to Fuyang in northern Anhui Province have colluded with local bandits, causing Yingxian, across hundreds of li, to suffer successively. The bandit flags are red with white borders, the symbols are red on top and white on the bottom, and there are thousands of men and women hostages. The military authorities of Henan and Anhui provinces have paid extraordinary attention to this group of defeated soldiers and bandits and have deployed capable troops to jointly suppress them. It is now learned that Cheng Ziyi's troops, the Bandit Suppression Commander of the Henan Army, have arrived at Zhuzhai and, together with Ni Lingge's battalion of the Anhui Provincial Security Force, repelled the defeated soldiers and bandits on the afternoon of the 10th. The bandits fled to the Sixty Mile Store between Fuyang Yingshang and Nan Zhao in the middle. The first and second regiments of the Anhui Provincial Security Force also departed from Zhengyang on the 12th and headed to the front line. At present, the bandit suppression troops have been fully equipped and will take a large encirclement formation to jointly suppress them. On the 12th, he accompanied Wu Xijun, the Deputy Director of the Provincial Security Department, on a warship to Yingshang for inspection and to inspect the defense of the upper reaches of the Huaihe River. At a time when the defeated soldiers and bandits in Fuyang and Yingxian were causing trouble, the Red bandits in Huoqiu County were also rampant. Huoqiu is located south of Yingshang County and suffered greatly from the Red bandits last year. It was later recovered by government troops, but the remaining bandits were not completely eliminated. After Xu Tingyao's troops returned in triumph, the bandits stirred up trouble again. Recently, taking advantage of the rampant bandits in Fuyang, they gathered more than two thousand people, with more than one thousand guns, several mortars, and several machine guns, and fled north from Yejiaji, hoping to harass Zhengyang in conjunction with the forces of Zhang Xueliang and Yang Yaode. A few days ago, they were severely suppressed by the Cheng Yi regiment of the Independent 40th Division of Xu Zhongyue's troops stationed in the county in the Maocaodian and Chen Linzi areas west of the Shi River. More than a hundred bandits were killed and countless were injured. The Cheng Yi regiment took advantage of the victory to advance to Sanbuguan Fuginshan, and then defeated the Red bandits. The troops stationed in Huoqiu County City, believing that both the northern and southern bandits have not been eliminated, in addition to sending teams to block and suppress them, have also strictly prepared in the city. (August 12th)

Special Report: Li Zhun's Naval Inspection Record 93

Recently, the French navy's occupation of nine islands in Hainan has caused international disputes. Now, our country has historically and geographically proven that these nine islands are indeed our territory, that is, belonging to the Xisha Islands, and are subordinate to Qiongya. In April of the 32nd year of the Guangxu reign of the former Qing Dynasty, Zhang Renjun, the Governor-General of Guangdong and Guangxi, fearing that the Japanese were plotting to occupy the Dongsha Islands, sent Li Zhisheng, the Guangdong Naval Admiral, to negotiate. Later, Mr. Li took the warships "Fubo" and "Chenhang" on a southern patrol, departing from Yulin Port in Yai. The next day, they arrived at Coral Island (Mr. Li renamed it Fubo Island). In total, they discovered 14 islands, which are the Xisha Islands. The islands that the French navy is forcibly occupying are also these. Mr. Li wrote a naval inspection record, detailing the journey, which is urgently reprinted here to prove that the Xisha Islands are indeed our territory.

After the Dongsha Island case was settled, I thought that there must be many islands in Guangdong like Dongsha. Lin Jun Guoxiang, the left-wing commander, who was experienced in navigation, said to me, "About two hundred nautical miles west of Yulin Port in Qiongzhou, there are islands, which Westerners call Paracel Islands (that is, PARACEL'S). About four hundred nautical miles from Hong Kong, anyone traveling east from Singapore to Hong Kong must pass this line. However, there are many reefs there, so ships often avoid it." I was eager to explore its details, include it in the nautical chart, and make it Chinese territory. Therefore, I requested Master An (that is, Zhang Renjun, the Governor-General of Guangdong and Guangxi, whose style name was Anpu) to explore this remote island. Master An readily agreed with my suggestion, and other enthusiasts among my colleagues also wanted to go and see it. Therefore, the task of naval exploration was assigned to Lin Jun Guoxiang, who took the warships "Fubo" and "Chenhang." Lin Jun said, "These two ships are too old and slow. If the weather is good, we can guarantee safety, but if we encounter strong winds, it will be very dangerous." I was eager to go, so I did not care about the risks. Therefore, I went on board with Lin Jun to examine the ship's boiler and machinery, repaired what needed to be repaired, and inspected all the masts, sails, and ropes. All the iron chains at the bottom of the cabin were pulled out onto the deck. Lin Jun tapped them with a hammer, and any chains that sounded damaged were marked with a white powder line to prevent them from breaking. Hundreds of dan of rice were prepared, as well as other livestock such as cattle, sheep, pigs, and chickens, canned food, and soda water. Various types of rice, sorghum, wheat, and bean seeds were also prepared.

The freshwater tanks were filled with fresh water, and the coal bunkers were filled with bituminous coal. In addition to the crew, one hundred laborers, carpenters, stonemasons, caulkers, and painters were hired, as well as wood, masts, flags, etc. The intention was to find these islands and colonize them. I brought a platoon of guards, led by platoon leader Fan Lianzhong. Wu Jun Jingrong was the captain of "Fubo," and Liu Jun Yikuan was the captain of "Chenhang." I rode on "Fubo," with Lin Jun in charge of navigation, and I listened to his commands. Wang Jun Rentang accompanied us to consult. Those traveling with us were Li Zichuan, the Observer (Zhejuan); Wang Shuwu, the Prefect (Wen ○); Ding Shaosun, the Prefect (Naicheng); Pei Daiyun, the Prefect (Zuze); Wang Daoyuan, the Magistrate (Zongzhu); Shao Shuiqiao, the Circuit Intendant (Siyuan); Liu Ziyi, the Magistrate; Mr. Browns, the German wireless engineer; and Mr. Booth, the manager of the Lihe Foreign Firm. We set off on April 2nd of the 33rd year. On the 3rd, we arrived at the waters of Qiongzhou and purchased fish and vegetables to replenish fresh water. The local officials came to welcome us, and we spent a day and a night socializing. On the 4th afternoon, we set sail and traveled south along Qiongzhou Island. On the 5th, we entered Yulin Port in Yazhou. A gentle breeze was blowing. I was on the deck, observing. I saw that the mountains, water, and terrain of this port were excellent, and the water depth was 20 to 30 feet. The entrance was less than three li wide. After anchoring, we were surrounded by mountains, but there was no water outlet. It was truly a good harbor for sheltering from the wind. However, the area was too small to accommodate many warships. Seven or eight ships would be insufficient for maneuvering. The water in the port was calm, and the surface was clear and vast. I thought that we could sail directly to the Xisha Islands. Guoxiang said, "The weather cannot be relied upon. We must look at the astronomy. We need three to five days of southwest wind to set sail. We also need to replenish fresh water here." A short time later, we went ashore with the other officials, each carrying a wooden stick to lean on while walking and to defend against animals. This was Guoxiang's advice. I thought that it was possible to defend against beasts, but how could birds harm people? Guoxiang said, "There are many large crows on the Xisha Islands. They are not afraid of people and even fight with people. Without these sticks, we cannot defend against them." After going ashore, we walked along the plain into the mountains. All along the way, there were coconut trees everywhere, laden with fruit, some as large as an embrace and about one hundred feet tall. They were as straight as palms, and the leaves were large like banana leaves but split and not connected. At that time, the weather was hot, and the travelers were thirsty. They shot the coconut trees with guns, and the fruits fell one after another. People picked them up, and if they were pierced by bullets, the juice flowed out. They drank it with their mouths, and it was sweet and smooth, a holy product for quenching thirst. After walking about six or seven li, we found residents, with disheveled hair and bare feet, without clothes, using cloth to cover their lower bodies. They were as black as lacquer, with hair all over their chests, backs, elbows, and legs. Their ears were pierced with iron rings, as large as the mouth of a rice bowl. It was easy to distinguish the old from the young, but difficult to distinguish men from women. Their dwellings were made of coconut trees, less than ten feet high and about one or two zhang wide. The beams, doorposts, and pillars were all coconut trees. The roof and walls were all made of thick screens woven from coconut leaves in a herringbone pattern. There were doors but no windows. The floor inside was also covered with coconut mats, several inches thick. There were no tables, beds, or curtains. They ate, lived, and slept there. I took pictures of them with a hand mirror, and they all smiled happily. Then we went to a place where many men and women were dancing in the fields. Old and strong people were playing gongs, flutes, and percussion instruments on the side. There were mostly women dancing, and sometimes men joined them, all young people. Their teeth were white, and their mouths were spitting red foam. We learned that they were chewing betel nuts. If a man and woman dancing liked each other, they would hold hands and return home as husband and wife. Their language was indistinguishable. Guoxiang could understand one or two words, as they were raw Li people from the mountains. Soon, we found a familiar Li person who could speak Chinese to act as an interpreter. According to him, there were many deer in the mountains, as large as horses, which could be used for transportation, so they were called deer-horses. I was eager to hunt, but I had no hunting dogs. The familiar Li person said that Li people could be used instead. I immediately ordered this familiar Li person to find several people to lead the way and drive the deer-horses. The raw Li people held a stick and moved as fast as flying. They stepped over the wooden stakes in the mountains, which were as sharp as knives, as if walking on flat ground. I led many guards to follow behind, extremely exhausted. I sat by a stone to rest for a while and lit a cigarette. A herd of deer rushed out of the forest, as large as cattle and horses. I shot at them with a gun, hitting one, which fell to the ground and got up again. The guards caught it. Its horns were as large as bowls and about three feet long. I shot three or four more times. When it fell to the ground, it broke a horn, and blood dripped out. A guard sucked it with his mouth. Then five or six people carried it back to the ship with a large piece of wood, weighing it at four hundred jin after removing the skin. They divided the meat to eat, and the velvet was hung on the deck to be blown by the wind, thinking it could be preserved. After a few days, it was maggot-infested and rotten, and the stench was unbearable, so it was discarded into the sea. One day after the rain, I was sitting on the deck in a high place, enjoying the cool. Suddenly, I saw a black object coming towards my ship from the sea, raising its head above the water. Its mouth was sharp and long. I asked, "What is this?" Guoxiang said, "This is a sea eel. Han Wengong (Han Yu) wrote an essay to drive them away in Chaozhou. This is the one." As he spoke, the sea eel reached the side of the ship and climbed up the rope ladder. I ordered the guards at the ladder to strike it with a gun, but the guards retreated several steps, not daring to strike. I quickly went down, seized a gun, and struck it. The sea eel fell, its white belly facing the sky, about forty or fifty feet from the ship. I immediately ordered the sailors to launch a sampan to catch it. The sailors used a pole to pick it up, but it was about ten feet long and too heavy to lift. Fearing that it was not dead, they did not dare to touch it. They fired two more shots, and it sank to the bottom of the water and disappeared. For several days, the weather was not good. A halo appeared around the moon, indicating that a strong wind was coming. Guoxiang bought countless firewood here, piled on the deck like a mountain, to be used when coal was lacking. He also bought hundreds of coconut mats from the Li people to build walls, roofs, and floors. On the fourth day, we gathered with our colleagues to visit the salt fields in Sanliao Port, about twenty li from here. We used rattan chairs strung with bamboo poles to walk, and hired Li people to carry us, agreeing to pay each person two mao of silver. The Li people were very strong and walked very fast, but they were not good at carrying, so the journey was very dangerous. In a short time, we arrived at the place. The salt fields were between two mountains, stretching for more than ten li, all salt fields. The water was extremely salty, and salt could be formed in one day. Some took two or three days, but it was not as common as in other salt fields. The price was extremely cheap, only two or three hundred coins per stone. Therefore, the smuggled salt in Hong Kong and Macau was all transported from here. In the forests along the way, there were many red and green parrots, of different sizes. The white ones were larger and fewer. There were also many small monkeys flying around, impossible to catch. After returning to Yulin Port, the Li people who carried the sedan chairs were given two mao of silver each, but they refused to accept it, because they wanted more. We increased it to four mao, but they still refused. After asking, we learned that they thought the price was two mao for each sedan chair shared by two people. Now that they were given two mao more, they refused to accept it. They were so simple and unsophisticated, truly like the people of ancient times. A Li person carried a large python on a bamboo pole to sell, and we gave him two yuan of silver and told him to take it away. They also carried several jars of rice wine, giving them one yuan of silver for each jar. The color was black and the taste was sweet. There were also Hui people from here, speaking a northern dialect, selling stone crabs and flying snakes. Few of the stone crabs were intact. Preserved in vinegar, they could treat sores. Flying snakes could induce labor. People competed to buy them. There was also a kind of coconut bead, like a fish eye, said to be formed inside a coconut shell after hundreds of years. Daiyun bought it. The Hui people said that they were left behind by Ma Fubo during his campaign against Jiaozhi. There were not many people left today, but they still spoke a northern dialect, different from the Cantonese. Guoxiang said that the weather was good and we could set sail. On April 11th, at four o'clock in the afternoon, we lifted anchor and left the port. The wind was calm and the waves were gentle. At seven o'clock, we suddenly saw something like an island in front of us, faintly visible. Guoxiang said, "There are no mountains here. It must be a whale. We should detour to avoid it." I looked at it with a telescope and saw a black shadow stretching across the water, not very high. My colleagues were eager to see it. Soon, it gradually sank. The ship continued to sail straight according to the longitude and latitude. Guoxiang and Jingrong stayed up all night, working on the deck, directing the helmsman. There was also a person on the top of the mast, observing with a telescope. They did not dare to relax at all. Guoxiang said, "According to the ship's speed and the sea conditions, we should be able to see the nearest island by now. If we don't see it, there must be an error in the astronomical measurement. Advancing one degree is very dangerous. This is because the ship's horsepower is insufficient and we have been pushed down by the current. We should be careful. There are many reefs here. If we are not careful, the whole ship will be smashed to pieces." A moment later, the person on the mast reported that he saw a black shadow, but it was upstream. Guoxiang and Jingrong carefully oriented themselves and steered straight towards the shadowy island. (To be continued)

Local News

Unemployed Overseas Chinese Return to Shanghai Yesterday 94

Government Allocates Funds to Transport in Batches

First Batch of One Hundred and Twenty-Three People

Distressed Return Home Recounting Past Hardships

(Shen Shi News Agency, Local Report) Hundreds of overseas Chinese in Japan, unable to withstand the oppression of that country, have become unemployed one after another. The Executive Yuan ordered the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission to work with the local consulate to shelter the unemployed overseas Chinese forced to leave Japan and send them back to their home country in batches. The first batch of one hundred and twenty-three men, women, and children arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning at six o'clock aboard the Changxing Company's "Asia Queen" ship. Details are as follows:

Reasons for Repatriation 95

Our country's overseas Chinese merchants are being squeezed and hated by the Japanese, and the number of unemployed is increasing day by day. Because they have no money to return home, they are displaced and suffer unspeakable pain. Later, the government initiated a plan in the spring of the 21st year of the Republic to transport unemployed overseas Chinese forced to leave Kobe and Yokohama back to their home country. However, Nagasaki had a larger population and various difficulties, so they were not immediately transported back. Recently, the Nagasaki branch of the Chinese Nationalist Party, seeing that a large number of unemployed overseas Chinese were stranded in a foreign country, with their livelihoods on the verge of collapse, and the Japanese oppression was severe, felt that if they were not quickly transported back, the future would be unthinkable. Therefore, they telegraphed the Central Overseas Party Committee to report everything. The Central Overseas Party Committee then wrote to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, which was approved by the Executive Yuan. The Ministry of Finance allocated more than six thousand yuan to begin transporting more than four hundred unemployed overseas Chinese in that area back to their home country in batches, to be sent back to their original homes separately.

Overseas Chinese Association Sends Personnel to Assist 96

After receiving the order from the Executive Yuan, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission originally intended to send personnel to Japan to handle all assistance matters. However, due to economic reasons, they had to entrust the Changxing Shipping Company and the Chinese Consulate in Nagasaki to handle the matter. The Commission recently received a reply from the Nagasaki Consulate stating, "To the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, Regarding the return of 123 overseas Chinese this time, 109 are going to Fujian, and Yang Hechai and Zheng Xingbang are designated as assistants. Eleven are going to Shandong, and three are going to Shanghai. Wu Zhenting is designated as the assistant. We hereby request that you provide assistance. Zhang Chi, Consul in Nagasaki, August 22nd." After receiving the telegram, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission immediately appointed Zhou Yanming, Director of the Administration Office, Zhao Xuanyang, and Tan Zhonglu to come to Shanghai from Nanjing to prepare all registration, assistance, and repatriation matters.

Situation of Overseas Chinese Arriving in Port 97

This first batch of returning overseas Chinese consists of 123 people, including 56 workers, 15 women and children, and 52 children. They arrived in Shanghai aboard the British-owned Changxing Company's "Asia Queen" ship. The ship entered the port at four o'clock yesterday morning and arrived at the Pudong Wharf at about six o'clock. At about nine o'clock, a small boat transported all the overseas Chinese to the Xinguang Wharf to disembark. Because of the large number of people and their disheveled appearance and mismatched clothing, the overseas Chinese were once interfered with by Western police officers. After the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission sent personnel to explain the situation, they were allowed to pass. After leaving Xinguang, the overseas Chinese took four pre-hired large trucks to the Asia Hotel on Avenue Edward VII, where dozens of rooms were arranged for them to stay. Meals were immediately provided. Because the returning overseas Chinese were all returning with their families, their luggage was extremely cumbersome. It was not until about eleven o'clock that the unloading was completed. The Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission will conduct a detailed registration of the returning overseas Chinese, including their place of origin, age, occupation in Japan, family situation, and personal skills. Particular attention will be paid to the skills, so that there is a basis for future relief.

Repatriation to Original Homes Separately 98

They will stay at the Asia Hotel tonight, and starting today, they will be sent back to their original homes in batches as quickly as possible. Most of the returning overseas Chinese this time are from Fujian, and a small number are from Shandong. Once there are ships going to Fujian, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission will purchase tickets for them and send them off. Those going to Shandong will return home by train, and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission has written to the Ministry of Railways to allow them to travel for free or at a reduced fare.

List of Overseas Chinese Arriving in Shanghai 99

The first batch of forced, unemployed overseas Chinese returning from Japan includes 56 men, 15 women, and 52 children, for a total of 123 people. The names and places of origin are listed below. 109 people from Fujian: Wang Shengjin, Wang Asong, Wang Meixiang, Wang Xiangmei, Wang Xiasiang, Zheng Deliu, Zheng Chuzi, Zheng Zuozi, Zheng Fusong, Zheng Fuhe, Zheng Fuli, Guo Jiadeng, Wei Shizhuo, Ye Zechang, Lin Wenzi, Huang Yonghua, Guo Jiafa, Lin Shengquan, Chen Deyi, Lin Moulong, Lin Xisong, Lin Chunquan, Ye Yuansheng, Ye Lunchang, Xu Kexing, Lin Chenglong, Lin Zhengrui, Lin Sunli, Guo Xiaofa, Guo Jinsong, Guo Ajin, Ye Yijin, Xue Dongju, Wei Lijia, Yang Ruxiu, Yang Cai Zengsong, Jie Zhenghe, Yang Meisong, Yang Gongying, Yang Hechai, Fang Peiguan, Ye Xiasong, Lin Zhenhui, Lin Jinxi, Lin Quan, Lin Sushun, Lin Ziyan, Lin Senjin, Lin Mingfu, Wang Sunyan, Wang Linsong, Weng Shengjin, Weng Weizi, Weng Guisong, Lin Jinlian, Xue Shuijin, Lin Chen Haosong, Lin Aiying, Lin Hongen, Lin Hongchao, Lin Honghai, Lin Hongan, Lin Fuxiong, Lin Chongzi, Lin Wenlong, Lin Zhongtang, Lin Zhuosong, Xue Tianxu, Ye Shenjing, Zhao Wenxiang, Lin Meifan, Lin Guisong, Lin Zhengsong, Lin Hexing, Lin Yusong, Lin Qinhe, Xue Qigan, Yu Changhuang, Yu Kangsong, Zheng Xingbang, Yang Jialiang, Yang Xiu, Lin Wenzhong, Lin Chen Baozhen, Lin Aijin, Weng Xuntan, Weng Zhuangshi, Weng Jinhua, Weng Junzi, Weng Mingjun, Weng Mingxiang, Wang Changyin, Wang Zilai, Wang Laixing, Wang Okada Kogo, Yang Jiakun, Lin Yulin, Yang Haxi, Xu Qishui, Xu Yirun, Xu Yuping, Yang Kefu, Wang Laibao, Lin Xianghe. Eleven people from Shandong: Wu Zhenting, Wu Lishi, Wu Changdong, Wu Quanchun, Wu Fuan, Wu Chunxiang, Sun Xiaojun, Wang Fangjin, Liu Minghao, Chen Jidong, Jia Rongyuan. Two people from Yangzhou: Gao Fudong, Chen Qingrong. One person from Qingtian: Pan Zhixuan.

Recounting Forced Experiences 100

A reporter from the Shen Shi News Agency visited the Asia Hotel to learn the truth about the hardships faced by overseas Chinese in Japan. However, most of the overseas Chinese had been in Japan for many years and could no longer speak their native language. Finally, they found a porcelain repair worker from Fujian who could speak freely. Here is a record of his words: "I am a porcelain worker and have been in Japan for seven or eight years. At first, it was okay there, but in recent years, the Japanese have treated us very badly. They either abuse us or want to deport us back to our home country. For example, when the Japanese buy things from overseas Chinese, they often give us at most five mao for something that is clearly worth one yuan. If you reason with them, they will beat you, and we cannot fight back. Even if we go to the police station, the judgment will always be against us. When we go to the Chinese Consulate to ask for help, the consul also tells us that there is really nothing they can do. Also, in the countryside of Nagasaki, the Japanese often ambush us for no reason. Chinese people in Nagasaki opened a Huile Yuan restaurant. One day, some Japanese came and not only refused to pay for their food and drinks, but also started arguing. They all pulled out knives and stabbed them on the table, saying, "You Chinese killed our Japanese in Shanghai, so we must kill you Chinese in Japan." If it weren't for the fact that the wife of one of the waiters was Japanese, the whole family would have been completely harmed. There are many, many things like this. In short, the oppression we suffered in Japan was really too deep. We can't do business and we'll starve to death if we stay in a foreign country. So we have to return to our home country. We are very happy to be back in our home country, but I heard that Japanese people often kill Chinese people in China. I don't know if it's true. We are very grateful to the government for rescuing us, but we hope the government will also find a fundamental solution for us, because we are unemployed. There's still no solution when we return to our old home..."

Second Batch Coming Soon 101

Most of the overseas Chinese returning this time are workers and small business people, especially cloth merchants. Because they are scattered in the four villages of Nagasaki, it took time for the consul to gather them, so they can only come to Shanghai in batches. The rest who have not yet returned are still being notified by the consulate in Nagasaki to gather at the consulate, so that they can continue to be transported back to their home country. According to officials from the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, the second batch of overseas Chinese will arrive in Shanghai on the next Changxing Company ship, with about 200 people.

Song Ziwen's Return Date 102

Departing from Seattle on the 12th

Expected to Arrive in Shanghai on the 29th

Song Ziwen, Vice President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, was ordered to go abroad to participate in the Washington World Economic Conference and the London World Economic Conference, and toured European countries, making many observations. Mr. Song originally planned to return to China from Geneva on the Italian mail ship "Conte Rosso", but because of a trip to the United States to meet with President Roosevelt, he changed his plans to return home on the 12th on the Dollar Line's "President Jefferson" ship, departing from Seattle. According to the itinerary, he is expected to arrive in Shanghai on the 29th. At that time, the central government and various sectors will send personnel to the pier to offer a grand welcome.

Shanghai-Philippines Trial Flight Departed Yesterday Morning 103

= Arrived in Hong Kong at 4:15 PM =

= Continuing Flight from Hong Kong to Manila This Morning =

In order to prepare for direct flights between China and the United States, China National Aviation Corporation is now conducting a preliminary trial flight on the route between Shanghai and Manila, Philippines. At 5:23 yesterday morning, American director Mr. Bixby, accompanied by American pilots and a party of four, flew a Sikorsky aircraft from Longhua Airport for a trial flight. At 4:15 PM, they arrived safely in Hong Kong. After staying in Hong Kong for one night, they continued flying from Hong Kong this morning at 5 o'clock. According to the itinerary, they are expected to arrive in Manila at 3 PM today. Details are as follows:

Departing Personnel 104

The Shanghai-Philippines route is the initial segment of the company's planned Sino-US intermodal transport plan. It was originally scheduled to depart for a trial flight on the 12th of this month, but due to insufficient preparation, it was changed to yesterday morning. The four people traveling on the Sikorsky aircraft are American director Mr. Bixby, pilot Mr. Grosvenor, co-pilot and radio operator Mr. Eihammer, and Mr. Mairnel, representative of American United Company. However, Mr. Mairnel stayed in Hong Kong after arriving in Hong Kong, and the other three continued on.

Takeoff Situation 105

At 4:30 yesterday morning, the pilots and American director Mr. Bixby and the other three people, wearing yellow flight uniforms, took a car and drove to Longhua Airport. The pilot, Mr. Grosvenor, inspected all parts of the Sikorsky aircraft, which was parked in the center of the airport. At 4:50, four workers pushed the aircraft into the Huangpu River and removed the double wheels under the fuselage. The four pilots entered the cabin one after another and immediately started the engine. After about five minutes, at 5:10, the aircraft gradually took off from the river surface. After flying around the airport twice from Pudong, at 5:23, it flew south in a rush amidst cheers and applause from the entire airport.

Safely Arrived in Hong Kong 106

The Sikorsky aircraft, equipped with a shortwave radio, communicated with the Shanghai Coastal Radio Station of the Ministry of Transportation every half hour to report its progress along the coast. The local radio station received the following reports from the aircraft yesterday: It took off from Longhua at 5:23 AM, passed Wenzhou at 7:30 AM, Pingyang County at 8:00 AM, Fuyoshan Mountain at 8:30 AM, Leiqi Bay at 9:00 AM, and arrived in Fuzhou at 9:20 AM to refuel. It departed from Fuzhou at 11:15 AM, passed Pinghai Bay at 12:00 PM, Weitou Bay at 12:30 PM, Kongshikou at 1:00 PM, Tazi Mountain at 1:30 PM, Nanao Island at 2:00 PM, Jinghai Bay at 2:30 PM, Jiazijiao Cape at 3:00 PM, Zhelangjiao Cape at 3:30 PM, and arrived in Hong Kong at 4:15 PM. It plans to stay in Hong Kong overnight and continue its flight at 5:00 AM this morning.

Yesterday's test flight of the Sikorsky aircraft to the Philippines (Photos by Tianzhang Zunyong)

Arriving Today 107

According to the company's original itinerary, it will depart from Hong Kong at 5:00 AM this morning. If the weather is good along the way, it will pass the Dongsha Islands at 9:30 AM and reach Labrado in the Philippines at 1:00 PM. It plans to refuel there and then fly directly to the Gedad Naval Air Station near Manila. It plans to stay in the area for about four days before departing for Shanghai. According to the company, all sectors of Manila have sent telegrams expressing their warm welcome.

Li Du's Subordinate, Su Anren, Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 114

Chen Zongdai Leads Troops to Resist Japan and Recovers Several Counties

Ding Chao Captured by the Japanese and Killed in Changchun

The Northeast News Agency reports that after General Li Du, Commander-in-Chief of the Jilin Self-Defense Army, withdrew to Russia, Chen Zongdai took over command of his troops and continued to resist Japan. Su Anren, propaganda team leader of Li's army, was summoned by telegram from General Li and entered the country via Mishan. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday. A reporter from the Northeast News Agency interviewed Su at his lodging. He spoke in detail about the activities of the Northeast Volunteer Army and the inside story of the puppet state. The details are as follows:

Chen Takes Over Command of Li's Army 115

After General Li Du withdrew to Russia last winter, Chen Zongdai took over as acting commander-in-chief. He led soldiers in the Erdaodaohezi area south of Yilan and continued to resist Japan. He repeatedly engaged in fierce battles with the enemy and stubbornly defended Boli County and Jiamusi. Due to lack of ammunition and reinforcements, he withdrew to Mishan. He contacted Zhang Baohe, Shan Guiting, Gao Baoshan, and other units to besiege Mishan. After more than ten days of hard fighting, he withdrew to the Muling River line due to weakness. Chen was stationed in Hulin, planning a counterattack. He sent personnel to the Russian territory and obtained spiritual assistance from the Russians and sympathy from the Korean Independence Corps. In June of this year, he occupied Heizuizi and Baipaozi. The puppet army Guo brigade in Mishan had the intention of rebelling. The puppet army Tao brigade was defeated in the Battle of Heizuizi. The fact that several counties have not been lost is due to Chen's determination to resist Japan.

Gao's Troops Contact and Attack 116

Gao Yushan of the Jilin National Salvation Army Wang Delin's army was originally a commander of the Gouli Brigade. After General Li left the country, Gao's army was authorized to use good firearms. Gao's army killed three Japanese consuls and two translators stationed in Hulin in three days. Russians in Jiangdong congratulated Gao County Jin Baiqi, saying that the hearts of the Chinese people had not died. Gao also led 3,000 troops to attack Mishan, contacted Chen's army, and resolved the Raohe puppet army. Thousands of civilians in the county also helped Gao resist Japan. Chen and Gao's two armies totaled 30,000 troops. Zou's army was stationed in Hulin, with rear defenses in Raohe and Funing, with more than ten artillery pieces, more than twenty machine guns, and a source of ammunition, and could operate victoriously.

Activities of the Volunteer Army in Liaoning and Heilongjiang 117

In Yilan, Jiamusi, and Nandai Diaoling, there are Zhang Zhichao's Wuwei Team and the Self-Defense Army Li Huatang, totaling more than 10,000 people, with great momentum. Zhang Xihou, commander of the rear of the Self-Defense Army in Jiangbei, together with Sui County Magistrate Chen Dafan, Liu Bin's subordinate Xu Xun, Wuwei Commander Ru Youcai, and Yuan Fushan and Zang Jingzhi, engaged in fierce battles with the Japanese Iizuka Regiment and Obina Detachment in Suidong in March. The Japanese army suffered heavy casualties and are still active in the Suidong area. There are also tens of thousands of volunteer soldiers in Yitong, Shuangyang, Panshi, and Dunhua, led by Mao Zuobin, who have repeatedly frustrated the enemy's advance. Deng Tiemei's troops, who have resisted Japan most vigorously in Liaodong, are now actively disrupting various counties in Liaohai and destroying the South Manchuria Railway.

The Truth About Ding Chao's Death 118

General Ding Chao, Chairman of the Jilin Provincial Government, retreated to Hezhoubang last winter after Binqing was lost due to his inability to resist. He hoped to withdraw to Russia, but the rear road was cut off by the Japanese army, making it difficult to advance or retreat. He was surrounded by the Iizuka troops of the Japanese army and became a prisoner. More than half of the soldiers surrendered their weapons, while the rest joined the Volunteer Army. General Ding, along with his staff members Tong Heng and Zhang Letian, was escorted by the Japanese to Harbin. After being interrogated by Lieutenant General Hiromura of the Hirose Division, he was escorted to the puppet capital Changchun. In April of this year, he was assassinated by the Japanese in Changchun Park. His staff members were also killed. Alas, how tragic!

Inside Story of the Puppet Manchurian State 119

The violent Japanese adopted the old strategy of annexing Korea, seizing political, economic, and educational power in the puppet Manchurian state. The main personnel in each department are Japanese. The so-called Emperor Puyi is just a puppet. Regarding the economy of Manchuria, the Japanese indiscriminately issued puppet Central Bank banknotes and issued propaganda to encourage their use. In the puppet state's education, Japanese language is added to all major and minor schools, and the youth are anesthetized with the fallacy of coexistence and co-prosperity. Their methods are known to be vicious.

Japanese Military Reorganizes Puppet Army 120

In the past, the puppet army has now been reorganized and disbanded by the Japanese army. Divisions are reorganized into brigades, and brigades are reorganized into regiments. The ranks remain the same, but the power shifts. A Major General brigade commander only commands two battalions, and a Colonel regiment commander only commands four small companies. The Japanese army is stationed in fortresses, and the puppet army is stationed outside various cities. Ammunition is not issued because the Japanese still have concerns. Each brigade and regiment of the puppet army also hires Japanese chiefs of staff, instructors, and advisors to monitor the actions of the puppet army. The numbers of the puppet army are listed below. In the Yilan Road area, Yu Nicheng and others have a total of 1,500 men. In the Binjiang Road area, Li Niwenbing has 2,500 men. In the Jichang Road area, Xing Nilian has 1,500 men. In the Yanji Road area, there is an independent regiment with 2,000 men. Zhang Nihaipeng has 5,000 men, and Yu Nizhishan has 3,000 men. The military strength cannot be concentrated, and the ammunition is insufficient. Without the cover of the Japanese army, they are not worth a single blow. Recently, those who fill the ranks of lower-level officers and soldiers in the puppet army are all driven by livelihood and have long had the determination to defect and support the advance of the Volunteer Army, which can be shown during combat. They cannot bear to kill each other. The soldiers all have a concept of their homeland. Whenever puppet officials give speeches with words of friendship with Japan, the soldiers scold them endlessly. Therefore, there are many who surrender.

Black Ships Fly National Flags 121

The puppet ships on the Songhua River, except for those forcibly seized by the Japanese army for military use, only have a few small merchant ships left. Whenever military or commercial transport passes through Tongjiang on the Ussuri River, they must raise the Qing Tian Bai Ri flag to pass. If they fly the puppet flag, the Russian side will stop them or detain them. The detention of the Tongshan ship was due to this reason. Recently, the areas bordering Russia on the Heilongjiang and Ussuri Rivers are neutral zones. The Japanese army cannot invade without authorization, and the Volunteer Army can take advantage of this opportunity to operate.

Zhu Jiqing Talks About the Course of the Volunteer Army's Resistance Against Japan 123

This Trip South is to Publicize the Accounts of Donations

Whether to Recover Lost Territory Depends on the Will of the People

Zhu Jiqing, Commander-in-Chief of the Northeast People's Salvation Army, went north to resist Japan last spring and made outstanding achievements in the Liaoxi-Rehe border area. After Tang Yulin abandoned Rehe and surrendered to the puppet Manchuria, Zhu led his troops to retreat to Xiaojiadian and continued to command the volunteer armies in Liaoxi-Rehe, lying in wait in various places on the Liaoxi-Rehe border, waiting for an opportunity to resist Japan. Recently, he decided to publicize the detailed accounts of the donations received from the people so that all sectors could understand the truth. He specially went south a few days ago. When he passed through Beijing, he met with President Wang and the central authorities to request instructions on future plans. Now that the publicity is complete, he arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning to prepare to publicize the various accounts. A reporter from this newspaper specially visited Zhu's private residence last night to inquire about the course of the Volunteer Army's resistance against Japan and its current situation. According to him, he went to the Liaoxi-Rehe border area in January of last year to engage in anti-Japanese work. The volunteer armies in Liaoxi and Rehe are directly under the command of the Northeast National Salvation Army Headquarters, so there are many of them. The first attack on Yixian last spring was undertaken by the troops of Ma Zidan and Li Haifeng. They fought the Japanese puppets and retreated after one day, with no major losses on either side. The second attack on Yixian Jinzhou was undertaken by the troops of Bao Enfu, Ma Zidan, Liu Chunqi, Mi Ziheng, Wang Yuanping, Meng Xiyao, Shi Linge, Li Peizhi, Zhang Zisheng, and Zhan Tao, totaling tens of thousands of people who engaged in fierce battles with the enemy for one and a half days. In the end, they retreated due to lack of ammunition. The third attack on Jinzhou was undertaken by the troops of Song Jiuling, Li Shijun, He Xiangchen, Gu Degui, and others. They fought hard for two days and two nights, but the result was unsuccessful and they retreated. Although our army failed to achieve its goals due to various reasons in the second and third attacks, the damage to the Japanese puppet army was not insignificant. When Tang Yulin abandoned Rehe without a fight, Zhu immediately led a small number of troops to retreat to Xiaojiadian, while the remaining volunteer armies still lay dormant in their original locations to facilitate resistance at any time. Most of the volunteer armies under his command were bandits, followed by the civilian regiments. Among the bandit teams, Gao Pengzhen was the most famous, with more than 5,600 men and more than 5,300 guns. He made outstanding contributions in the battle to attack Xinmin. Zhu returned to Beijing once in July of last year and then went back to work outside the pass. He did not leave Xiaojiadian to go south until June of this year. After Zhu went south, he received reports that the Japanese puppet army in Yixian began to attack the volunteer army on July 6. The volunteer army rose up to resist and fought fiercely until July 18. Both sides suffered heavy casualties. Since the 18th, the fighting has stopped. The reporter asked how many volunteer soldiers there were in Liaoxi. Zhu replied that there were hundreds of thousands of people, and the guns were all ready, but they were all fighting independently, so they failed to achieve great results. The reporter asked, then is there a way to reorganize them? Zhu replied that the way to reorganize them is to gather the leaders of the various troops in one place and then reorganize them. However, the cost is huge, and it is quite difficult to limit resources. The reporter asked about the current situation of the volunteer army in Liaodong. Zhu replied that there were still many volunteer armies in Liaodong, such as the troops left behind by Wang Delin, with more than 20,000 people. In addition, there are many local militias everywhere, currently commanded by Deng Tiemei and Tang Juguwu, and they have all been launched one after another. Local newspapers have also reported on them, but their strength is still limited. Whether the lost territory can be recovered depends on the government's policies and the will of the people. Zhu came south specifically to publicize the accounts of donations received, and he is now scheduled to send them to the newspapers tonight (last night) so that all sectors can browse them tomorrow morning. Shanghai is very hot and he is not used to living there. The northern affairs are heavy and need to be dealt with urgently, so he will return north within a few days. The matters that should be contacted with the central government have been completed in Nanjing, so there is no need to go to Lushan again, and so on.
