Education News

Special Article on National Defense Education 194

(IV)

Central University Professor Zhang Qiyun's Speech at Tao Ji's Place

㈣ The greatest purpose of national defense education in rural communities is to enable students to deeply integrate into the people, using the organization of the military to organize society, which we simply call rural covenants. Covenant means restraint or organization. In December of the twentieth year of the Republic, Mr. Ma Xiangbo published a tearful appeal to young people, which expressed this meaning very earnestly. He said, "[The old man believes that the most urgent national salvation strategy today is to imitate the ancient system and implement the Baojia method, linking ten households into one Jia, ten Jia into one Zhongjia, ten Zhongjia into one Dajia, ten Dajia into one Tuan, ten Tuan into one Zhongtuan, and ten Zhongtuan into one Datuan. Extend this further, first creating a register of the population, follow the army's organization, so that its actions are uniform, command is swift, communication is tight, and will is firm. Guiding it to not cooperate with Japan is possible, guiding it to economic severance with Japan is possible, and guiding it to a desperate war with Japan is also possible. The old man has planned it, looking around at the rivers and mountains, I am endlessly saddened, and I hate myself for being old and weak, unable to repay the country, so I place my hopes on you, young students. The old man deeply believes that the country is based on the people, without responsible citizens, the country will have no way to stand. At the same time, I deeply believe that self-help is the only way to save oneself, and only self-help can break through the current difficulties. Seeking help from others, begging for mercy from others, are all in vain. Young people are the backbone of society and the pillars of the future of the country. I hope that we can be of one heart and one mind, and engage in arduous and effective struggle.]" According to Chinese history, it has repeatedly suffered from the invasion of foreign tribes, but the social foundation has been unusually solid, and has never been shaken, and has always achieved the final victory. This cannot but be attributed to the perfection of the ancient rural governance. Ancient rural governance had the Baojia method and the rural covenant method. Baojia was a strict rural organization, and the rural covenant promoted rural morality. This was the foundation of rural governance. There were also community granaries to enrich people's livelihood, and community schools to correct people's morality. Community granaries represented the economic aspect, and community schools represented the educational aspect. In addition, there were village communities representing the religious aspect, totaling five major departments. The undertakings contained in modern local autonomy are only these few, but the names are renewed. Ancient Chinese rural governance attached the greatest importance to the rural covenant system, in order to have leaders with noble character in the countryside, who could use the organization of the army to organize society. I once said in a speech in Chinese Youth China, "[I believe that local autonomy] is an extremely important position in secondary education. Because middle school students are between being able to advance and retreat. If they advance to university, their studies in middle school will be the foundation for further study. Otherwise, if they serve the community, they should also use their knowledge to become the driving force for implementing local autonomy... I believe that graduates of middle schools should become the majority of thoughtful and moral rural people, or leaders of rural people. This is one of the most important missions of China's secondary education." The past cannot be admonished, but the future can still be pursued. Our hope lies entirely in young people, teaching them, educating them, cultivating their noble spirit, patriotic thought, strong will, and deep learning, then the humiliated motherland will have hope of revival.

Lecture Four: Military Training for Young People 195

In recent decades, China will be surrounded by a situation where war is unavoidable, and the whole country must have the determination to reorganize its military equipment and devote itself to the military training of young people. It is necessary to ensure that citizens, when receiving ordinary education, develop the qualifications of soldiers in their hometowns, and these soldiers in their hometowns will then train local reserve forces. Once something happens, no matter where, they will instantly become a formidable enemy. What was most lacking in the European war was manpower. China is not like this now. The number of people who can be and are willing to be volunteers is definitely not small. What is most lacking at present is the talent for military command and organization. A national army is a army of the people, so officers must also be nationalized, that is, in addition to central officers, there must be a large number of local officers or civilian officers to supplement the shortfall. All countries in Europe and the United States have a system of civilian officers, which China can modify and transplant. The time spent by civilian officers accounts for only a small part of their lives, and in the remaining years, they can still indulge in managing their production undertakings, which is called soldiers among farmers or soldiers among workers. In this way, the majority of officers can support themselves, which can reduce the significant burden on national finances. Such soldiers in their hometowns usually promote national defense concepts and strive to bring the military and civilians closer, so that soldiers and the people are integrated into one. When the country is in trouble, spiritual and material support can be endless, and the power of national defense can be infinitely great. Even if the initial war is defeated, and the local defense line is retreated, there is still room for a comeback. Such a large country as China, even if it loses the border provinces, or even if it loses a large metropolis, it cannot determine its death, nor can it stop it from fighting again. The enemy cannot but worry that once the entire Chinese people rise up to counterattack, they will turn defeat into victory. Who is responsible for the military training of young people? This is, of course, the responsibility of central officers. Central officers refer to professional officers who serve for life, and there are specially established central officer schools, which will not be mentioned here. The Supreme Command of the National Army, in accordance with the provisions of the Organic Law of the National Government, belongs entirely to the National Government. All construction, maintenance, and operation of the national army, navy, and air force, as well as all powers relating to military administration and military orders, are entirely controlled by the Central Supreme Military Organ, in order to ensure absolute military unity and that the state does not repeat the past mistakes of military power falling into the hands of others, and establishes a foundation for consolidating national power and enriching national defense. Therefore, civilian officers receive education and command from central officers above, and educate and command the masses below. Civilian officers have both educational and command responsibilities, because being able to educate but not being able to command makes it difficult to connect principles and applications, and schools and troops are separated into two paths. Being able to command but not being able to educate also makes it difficult to perfect the command. Mr. Jiang Baili said, "Only the Chinese say that a person is both civil and military, and Westerners have never said this. I have carefully considered this sentence and it seems to have a symptom. The fundamental reason for China's lack of progress may be due to this. Civil represents knowledge, and military represents power. Praising a person as both civil and military is no different from saying that ordinary people are not good at either, clearly stating that those with knowledge must not have power, and those with power must not have knowledge. If one possesses both, then it is truly rare and valuable. Try to think, if there is knowledge but no power, how can it be implemented, what is the use of knowledge? If there is power but no knowledge, how can it be distinguished, what is the value of power? People must have both knowledge and power, which is a complete talent, but this is an internal matter, so why praise it?"

Due to the limitation of homework on weekdays, students' military training is still not enough, so it is appropriate to use holidays to set up military research classes at the drill sites to study the necessary military academics, and not only on the ground, but also to conduct air and sea military training. Use holidays to train student pilots and student navigators. During the exercises, it is appropriate to assume that the national border is invaded by enemy countries, and study methods of response, such as the speed of mobilization and the agility of action, which can be practiced on the spot. Still fearing that the education of civilian officers is insufficient, the In-hometown Soldiers Association can be reorganized to serve as a central body for discussing military issues. If the sincerity of national defense is accumulated in the heart, then the appearance of heroic courage will be obvious on the outside. The organization of the In-hometown Soldiers Association is public and free. Whenever the government is about to establish military laws or implement a military administration, civilians may gather on their own to discuss it and present their opinions to the authorities. Even if the government has established a law or implemented a policy, it also engages in discussions. If it is right or wrong, continue to ask questions, and then advertise it in the newspapers. The meeting place is in the school, and the discussion of military academics is like discussing philosophy, history, law, and politics, etc. The thinking is active, the will is free, and military magazines are published to publish academic progress. Once the atmosphere is opened, it can naturally give China's military a new face and spirit. Military scholars are only a part of life knowledge, and the connection between this part and other parts must be known. The analysis of this part and the synthesis of the whole must be known. In the past and present, the military officers who can become generals are all rich in ordinary knowledge, can represent the trends of the times, and show the correct direction of life. Those who are uneducated cannot become famous generals.

Former US President Roosevelt, in a speech in San Francisco, promoted military nationalism, saying that he did not want the United States to become Chinafied. Is Chinese culture not permanently suitable for survival in the world? This is a very sad thing to hear, but we can now only use Japan's established facts to defend Mr. Roosevelt's fallacy, which is even more sad. Chinese culture rose from Confucius, and for the subsequent 2,400 years, it has been relied upon by all countries in East Asia. In terms of its form, it is somewhat like a religion, (the Japanese call Confucianism Confucianism), but Confucianism says more about worldly morality, unlike religion, which focuses on transcendent concepts. Confucianism and science go hand in hand without contradicting each other. Its breadth is even greater than that of religion. According to the Japanese scholar Inoue Tetsujiro, Confucianism is a major element of the Meiji education. The cultivation of virtues such as loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, and righteousness, from the spiritual melting and pottery of the Japanese national character, the influence of Confucianism is the greatest. The purpose of Confucianism is to cultivate morality, use the great spirit of individuals to encourage the will of the masses, and today, it is to focus on the cultivation of personality. At the time of the Meiji Restoration, those who were active and dedicated to the development of the new civilization were mostly Confucian scholars. These patriots did not belong to the Zhu Zi school, but to the Yangming school. The Yangming school was smaller in number but produced more heroes, and was the original driving force of the Meiji Restoration. The Yangming school is based on conscience. If conscience sees it as good and righteous, it will definitely implement it. It is more biased towards subjective judgment, regardless of the circumstances in which it is located. Although not without drawbacks, it is rich in the spirit of practice, which is truly enjoyable. Du Xigui went to Japan to inspect the navy, and once visited the naval vice-minister Yamanashi. Yamanashi said that in ancient Chinese books, such as Sun Wu's Art of War, the study of strategy is profound and exquisite, and cannot be compared with modern German strategic books. Now, many students in our country (referring to Japan) study Chinese military books in the army and navy. Marshal Togo is a worshiper of Mr. Wang Yangming. The doctrines of Yangming are admired by Japanese scholars and officials. Du said that when he heard these words, he could not help but sweat profusely.

Today, China's national spirit is declining, and the soul is disappearing. It is impossible to promote the vitality of the army and invigorate the spirit of the army without promoting Confucianism. Confucianism is the national soul of China and the original driving force of all reforms. The greatest sorrow is the death of the heart. China's national heart is on the verge of death. New Confucianism is the only good way to revive this dying national soul. For more than two thousand years, there have been many people like Wang Yangming. How many lessons have been learned in history? Confucianism in China is not only a glorious legacy, but a legacy of strength. The way to restore vitality and the way to encourage courage and victory lies in this. The Chinese people only know that Japan has occupied our territory, but they do not know that before the Japanese army occupied our territory, it first occupied the strategies and tactics of our Mr. Wang Yangming, etc. In recent decades, Japan has studied Wang Yangming, while we have studied Japan. It is a strange thing. Why not directly study our inherent Wang Yangming instead of indirectly studying Wang Yangming? The legacy of Confucius, we do not know how to inherit ourselves, so that it falls into the hands of others, and others use it to attack and defeat us. Abandoning our inherent national treasures and picking up the remains of others is the most painful thing in the world. Military education, the Japanese do it, and they win our country in one fell swoop, and then win the powerful Russia, and dominate East Asia. We do it in our country, but it only creates a situation of chaos and danger, because one is for the country, one is for personal gain, one is for unity, and one is for dispersion. Asking the reason, one cannot help but sigh and hate the general public in China for abandoning the old studies as a common problem. Although the Japanese nation receives Western culture and understands Western academics, it cannot be without its own cultivation. This cultivation comes from Confucianism. Confucius said, "I do not enlighten those who are not eager to learn, nor do I teach those who are not eager to speak." Now that everyone is enthusiastically promoting military training for young people, we cannot help but loudly appeal to awaken our dying national soul. (End)

Jiangxi Province Middle School Graduation

Statistics of Entrance Examination Results 197

High School Entrance Examination Number: 254 people

│ Passing: 104 people │

│ Passing: 837 people │

The Jiangxi Province Middle School Student Graduation Entrance Examination was held simultaneously in six regions on June 26th. The process was relatively smooth. All test papers from the regions have been delivered one after another, and the grading has been completed in order. In addition to the students who were retained and those who passed, students who failed in one or two subjects will be allowed to retake the exam once in accordance with the regulations. Due to the vast area, the procedures for this retake, such as drafting questions, printing questions, and sealing and distributing test questions, are extremely strict and cumbersome, and take a lot of time. Therefore, the results of the retake will not be announced until the middle of this month. Because the students who are retaking the exam are between retained and passed, it is difficult to make a decision until all procedures have been completed. The statistics of the confirmed results of the examination are as follows: In the first district (Nanchang), the number of students taking the entrance examination was 134 in high school and 789 in junior high school. Fourth Broadcast for National Salvation by the University Federation 202

Lecture by Liu Xuru of Great China University

The fourth broadcast for national salvation by the Shanghai University Student Union was held yesterday at 5:00 PM at the Sino-Western Pharmacy radio station. Liu Xuru of Great China University delivered a speech titled "The Responsibility and Future of Chinese Youth," the content of which briefly stated: (I) The Chinese nation is at a critical juncture of life and death. Youth are the lifeline of the country and the vanguard of the nation, and should urgently invigorate their spirits, unite their strength, promote the awakening of national consciousness throughout the country, and shoulder the heavy responsibility of saving society, the country, and the nation. (II) The youth community should promote three kinds of spirit: (A) Promote the spirit of hard work and endurance, and eliminate the habits of decadence and extravagance; (B) Promote the spirit of proactive advancement and eliminate the attitude of negativity and timidity; (C) Promote a sense of responsibility to society and change the attitude of making empty talk and not taking responsibility. (III) The direction of Chinese youth's efforts is the future of the Chinese nation. They should take the Three Principles of the People as a guideline and strive for the movement to save China without departing from the nationalistic standpoint and without violating the principles of socialism. The speech lasted about thirty minutes and was very insightful.

National Shanghai College of Commerce

Preparation for the Transition of New and Old Presidents 203

The National Shanghai College of Commerce in this city, reorganized from the former Business School of National Central University, has always had a good academic atmosphere. However, last autumn, a "Reinstatement Committee" was suddenly organized by the students, and a student strike broke out. Recently, due to the students' excessive actions, the Ministry of Education ordered strict measures to be taken. After deliberation by the college affairs meeting, several students were expelled, which led to attacks on President Xu. Consequently, the Ministry of Education expressed dissatisfaction with Xu, which is the reason for Xu's resignation. It is now known that the newly appointed President Pei Fuheng has arrived in Shanghai and is preparing to take over. Mr. Xu returned to Shanghai yesterday and instructed his staff to prepare for the handover. The text of Mr. Xu's letter to President Pei is reproduced below: [Addressed directly], Received your letter of August 8, informing that you have been appointed by the Ministry of Education as the President of the National Shanghai College of Commerce and instructing me to hand over the affairs, which I have read with respect. Commercial Library of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce 206

Admission to Read Requires a Reader's Card

The Commercial Library of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce has been established for eleven years and has spared no effort in collecting newly published books and magazines. Therefore, more than one hundred people come to the library to read every day. According to the library's usual practice, those who come to the library to read must first fill out an introduction card, which the library exchanges for a reader's card, and then they can enter the library to read. Previously, for the convenience of general readers, the reader's card system was once abolished. However, the library is a public institution, and the people who come to read are from all walks of life, with varying levels of quality, which is unavoidable. It is heard that the library has now restored the reader's card system to show a slight restriction. It is hoped that readers will bring their reader's cards with them when they go to the library in the future to facilitate inspection. Those who do not have a reader's card can ask the library for an introduction card, fill it out according to the format, and exchange it for a reader's card for reading at any time.

Hong Kong-Honolulu Overseas Chinese Baseball Match 214

Hong Kong Wins the First Game Eight to Six

Fighting Broke Out in the Second Game

(Hong Kong Correspondent) At 4:00 PM on the 5th, a special softball game was held at the South China Stadium on Caroline Hill. The teams competing were the Honolulu Overseas Chinese team and the Hong Kong South China champions. The strengths of the two sides were evenly matched. Among the Honolulu team members were former representatives of our country's sport, such as Zheng Fa and Yu Bohui, whose skills had long been deeply impressed in our minds. As for the other members, they had also just returned from Honolulu. As for the two Chinese teams, in addition to the Zheng brothers playing for Honolulu, many had also returned from foreign countries. Zhou Longcan, Fang Shuotong, Fang Shuopei, and Chen Lunying returned from California, USA, while Bao Jianhong, Zheng Qingyang, and Zheng Biao returned from Japan. Judging from the above situation, it can be said that the forces were evenly matched, who would say otherwise?

In the game on the 6th, South China finally won eight to six in the ninth inning. It was not that the Honolulu team's skills were inferior to South China's, but rather that the Honolulu team was assembled in an instant and had not yet achieved the same level of coordination as South China. This special competition was a best-of-three series, and the Honolulu team had a great opportunity to counterattack. Although South China won, they could not rest easy. At 4:00 PM on the 7th, the two teams met again at the South China stadium. It was thought that there would be a more intense competition between the two teams, but unfortunately, a fight broke out in the middle, and the game ended unhappily, which is truly a pity. The details are recorded below:

In the first game, the entire battle situation was in a state of anxiety. Zheng Qingyang, who had returned from Japan, served as the pitcher for South China and performed admirably. Zhou Longcan's skills are already well known to the readers. Zheng Biao, Chen Lunying, and the Fang brothers were good at hitting and defending, giving the Honolulu team no chance at all. Wu Zhenbang and Bao Jianhong also performed brilliantly. In short, the South China team truly showed its artistry to the public. The Honolulu team, due to Lin Jinyou's absence, had Zheng Fa as the pitcher, who was also able to fulfill his duties. Gao Hannen, Yu Bohui, and Zheng Qiongren were particularly outstanding members of the team. It was only a pity that Liu, who was in charge of right field, lost several times.

In the second game of the Honolulu Overseas Chinese softball team, the original purpose of this special softball competition with the Hong Kong team was to connect feelings and improve skills. Unexpectedly, a fight broke out between the two sides at the beginning of the fourth inning, and a group of people were beaten. Even the peacemakers were affected. As a result, the game ended unhappily. The origin of the incident was that Zheng Qiongren, when at third base, wanted to steal back to his base, but he could not do it, so he returned to third base. At that time, he suddenly pointed at Chen Lunying, saying that he had kicked him. He then got up and beat Chen. Chen resisted, and the two fought each other. At that time, fellow soldiers who saw this wanted to stop it, but it caused misunderstandings among Zheng Xing and others, who thought they were helping Chen, so they suddenly came forward and beat him indiscriminately. Everyone then fought together. The witness, Meifeiao, was also punched in the face while trying to stop the fight. After several attempts to stop the fight, it was finally resolved, but the verbal arguments continued, and another disturbance almost broke out in the locker room. Zhou Longcan was punched in the face, and everyone left in a huff.

After the start of the game, the Honolulu team's first attack was unfavorable, and South China counterattacked. Zheng Biao hit a hit and got on base. Zhou Longcan sent him home, and Chen Lunying sacrificed to hit a home run. Zhou advanced to first base, and then stole third base. Fang Shuopei hit a ball, and Zhou stole home. Fang Shuotong then hit a hit, sending Chen home. Zheng Qingyang also got a hit, and Fang also went home. Bao Jianhong also got a hit, and Zheng also went home. In this inning, South China scored five points. In the second inning, neither side scored. In the third inning, the Honolulu team scored again, while South China scored two points by Fang Shuotong and Deng Qingyang. At the beginning of the fourth inning, Zheng Fa freely advanced to base, stole third base, and took advantage of Zheng Xing's hitting the ball to steal back to home base, but he could not do it, so he returned to third base. He suddenly pointed at Chen Lunying and said that he had kicked him, and a dispute arose, so the game was scattered. At that time, the score was South China winning by seven to one.

Yusa's result in the 200-meter freestyle semi-final was 2 minutes and 13 seconds, and his 100-meter freestyle semi-final time was 58 seconds, both of which were new Japanese records.

Kitamura Hisatoshi (Kochi Commercial), 19 minutes and 8 seconds (new Japanese record), 2. Makino Masazo (Waseda University), 19 minutes and 22.8 seconds, 3. Honda (Saint Paul's), 19 minutes and 39.6 seconds.

Page 19

Free Talk

Model Essays 220

— Xu Maoyong

Don Quixote went crazy from reading chivalry novels, so he became a knight-errant himself, righting wrongs. His relatives knew that it was the books that were to blame, so they asked the barber next door to inspect them. The barber selected a few good ones to keep, and the rest were burned.

Madam B, however, because she was moving, asked me to be the "barber" and "inspect" the books left by her father and brothers, "select a few good ones to keep," and prepare to "burn" the rest that were useless.

When I was inspecting, I found a book titled "Model Essays for Higher Primary School, Volume 4." It should have been in the "burn" list, but I happened to flip through it and saw that the second article was "On the Three Eastern Provinces." After reading it out of curiosity, I couldn't help but "slap the table and exclaim."

The full text is as follows:

"The existence of the Three Eastern Provinces to our country is like a dike to a river. If the dike collapses, the water will come. If the Three Eastern Provinces are lost, the country will perish. This is undeniable. After annexing Korea, the Japanese are eager to extend their hands to the Three Eastern Provinces, regarding them as objects in a bag. Now they openly declare to the public: whether by military force or by commercial teams, they must obtain them. Moreover, their ambition is even more rampant, wanting to invade Eastern Mongolia. Alas, Japanese, why are you willing to be the leader of barbarians, harming your own kind? What justice is there in this world? Bismarck said: "Iron and blood!" I also say: "To protect the Three Eastern Provinces in order to protect China, there is absolutely no hope without iron and blood." The new government is creating and managing, and has no time to devote to the defense of the Three Eastern Provinces. Only the people of the Three Eastern Provinces, born here, growing up here, and living here, how can they bear to be indifferent! Therefore, those who save the Three Eastern Provinces are the people of the Three Eastern Provinces. Those who lose the Three Eastern Provinces are also the people of the Three Eastern Provinces. Think about it, think about it, think about it seriously. Those who covet us, throw your life at them. Throw your life at them, and perhaps the Three Eastern Provinces may have a chance. Otherwise, once the defense is withdrawn, I fear that the whole country will perish with it. In that case, why should we care about this seven-foot body?"

This model essay was published by Shanghai Huiwentang. It is the "revised 16th edition in July of the third year of the Republic of China." The first edition was published in the first year of the Republic of China. The author is Shao Botang. However, according to "Postscript by Cai Cheng of Guyue," Shao Tang died during the "uprising in Chu," and was unable to "witness the republic." Therefore, the original work, where it did not conform to the times, was "reluctantly revised in several places" by Cai. This article "On the Three Eastern Provinces," which mentions the "new government," is also known to be by Cai.

The creation of this article was twenty-two years ago from now, and it is exactly twenty years since the fall of the Three Eastern Provinces. The "new government" mentioned in it is still the Yuan Shikai government. However, twenty years later, isn't the government still "having no time to devote to the defense of the Three Eastern Provinces"? Twenty years later, isn't the "world" still without "justice"? As for the Japanese ambition for Manchuria and Mongolia, the relationship between the Three Eastern Provinces and the whole country, and the need to resist aggression by force, all are accurate. In particular, the phrase "Those who lose the Three Eastern Provinces are also the people of the Three Eastern Provinces" is enough to make the young Marshal Zhang, who was "born here, grew up here, and lived here," bow his head without defense. "How can he bear to be indifferent," but who knew that he would actually be indifferent? What else is there to say!

In the two years since the September 18th Incident, I don't know how many grand and great works have appeared in newspapers and magazines, but who can match these mere two hundred and sixty-one characters from twenty years ago in terms of genuine knowledge and insight, and concise language?

From this, it can be seen that China does not lack people of insight. However, people of insight can only write essays. They have more than enough heart but not enough power. National affairs are managed by a different kind of people, so the crisis that was genuinely seen and foreseen twenty years ago finally led to the situation twenty years later, causing the people of twenty years ago to feel the pain of "unfortunately, my words came true."

But if an essay can be done like this, it can truly be a "model."

Talking About China's So-Called [Art Movement] 221

— Fu Yiye

In China, the art movement is as dark as the political movement. Artists (?) do not want the masses; they are only bent on having their own way, busy building up personal fame and fortune: today, they collude with several important people and celebrities to act as initiators, holding personal exhibitions; tomorrow, they will win over their own cronies and colleagues to run magazines, publish collections of paintings, and brag or mutually flatter each other: then they become masters and painting patriarchs. The achievements of the so-called art movement are only measured by the number of tickets sold for our painting patriarchs' and masters' painting exhibitions and the sales volume of painting collections. Therefore, the corruption in today's Chinese art world is no less than that on the political stage.

However, the real [art movement] is thus greatly misunderstood. Society only knows that someone is an artist, a master, a painting patriarch. And these painting patriarchs and masters are classified as a special class, just like important people and celebrities. As for their artistic accomplishments, what impact art has on society, and our demands and understanding of art, etc., there is no need to talk about it at all, because what the masters and painting patriarchs want is fame and fortune, and society only needs to recognize someone as a master and a painting patriarch, that's enough. The pursuit of fame and fortune and the worship of idols form the scene of the current art movement. This farce is staged year after year, except for making a few swindlers and rascals famous and rich, art will always be divorced from society. This can be seen from the fact that we have had a so-called art movement for nearly twenty years, and beautiful women's calendar posters are still welcomed there, and young artists returning from abroad have to change careers to paint advertisements for beer and cigarettes.

The Boss 222

— Cai Niensun

In the past six months, the boss's face has become more and more gloomy and terrifying.

In the past, although the boss had the air of every boss—majesty, there was sometimes a hint of a smile on his gray face full of smoking addiction; he also talked more, and his tone was gentle with majesty. For example, last year Lao Yu rushed home because his mother was seriously ill, without notifying the boss: when he came back, the boss only said: [In the future, you should tell me first]. No other nagging words.

In the past six months, the situation has been different. His face, that gray face, has no smile; the entire face looks gloomy. And his eyes radiate angry flames intertwined with anger and hatred, looking like he wants to eat people. He speaks very little, and it is always cold, giving people a feeling of severe cold. Every clerk is living in fear, and they are afraid when they see the boss's shadow.

The boss himself doesn't understand why he is so gloomy, he is just annoyed, annoyed that the cloth is not selling. His house is full of cloth that he has received successively in the past six months since the end of last year. He feels heartache when he sees the cloth; he is so heartbroken that he doesn't want to be at home, but he still spends most of his time in the cloth shop.

Every day, he sits as usual on the rattan chair next to the threshold, holding a water pipe and puffing away. At this time, there is silence in the shop. In front of the counter, it looks very deserted because no yarn has been released for half a year. Sometimes, it is rare for one or two rural women to bring cloth, and the clerk stretches lazily, cheers up a little, first measures the length, and then carefully looks at the thickness of the cloth, and in the comparison of the boss's eyes, returns the price: [One string and two! ] [One string and seven! Last month ·······] So the boss coldly opened his mouth aside: [A foot and two heads (Zhuang, that is, a local cloth with a one-foot and two-inch wide facade) I'll take it from you, and you still think it's too little! ] The rural woman argued several times, and finally sold it with heartache.

As the rural woman walked out of the shop, the boss complained sullenly: [People nowadays, what conscience do they have, one foot and two heads, which cloth shop would accept it? I'll take it from him, and they still argue about getting more and think it's too little! ]

The clerks also echoed, but in fact they knew very well in their hearts what was going on.

The cloth is not selling, not only the boss is anxious, but they are also really panicked. Since the Northeast hung up the Rising Sun flag, sales have plummeted. Following the economic decline of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, the cloth has also lost a corner of the market. Now there are only the three provinces of Fujian, Guangdong, and Shandong. Foreign cloth is so cheap, who would be happy to buy small, crude local cloth? In this situation, the cloth industry is indeed difficult to sustain, and if it doesn't close down, it will have to lay off a large number of people.

Qin and Zhang, who used to be good at talking, have also gradually become silent: this group of clerks just hope all day long, hoping that the smile on the boss's face will return.

But the boss's face is becoming more and more gloomy and terrifying day by day!

Maxims of La Bruyère 223

— Fu De

Some things in the world are most taboo to be ordinary, such as: poetry, music, painting, speech, etc.

The lives of heroes make history appear lively, and history makes the behavior of heroes appear beautiful; looking at it this way, should the person who writes history thank the hero who provided them with such lofty material, or should these heroes thank their historians?

The glory and achievements of some people lie in writing well, while others do not write a single word.

A fool reads a book and gets nothing. An ordinary person reads a book and thinks he understands everything. A wise man reads a book and sometimes cannot understand everything. He treats obscurity as obscurity, just as he treats clarity as clarity. A talented person reads a book and often treats clarity as obscurity, and insists on not understanding what is perfectly understandable.

A good and careful writer often feels that the words and sentences he spent a lot of time finding are the most simple and natural, and could have been thought of effortlessly at the beginning.

Ordinary Things (40) 224

— Dan Guosun

[Then I'm really sorry! Something happened at your residence, it seems the old gentleman doesn't know yet! ]

[Who are you talking about? ]

[Your respected father. ]

[My father? ]

[Yes, your respected father! ]

[How would my father know! I haven't seen him for two whole days! Have you seen him today? ]

[I have, the old gentleman is still at my house. ]

[Really? ] Bo Tang suddenly stood up, [Is it Chongqing Road? I was just about to talk to my father. ]

After saying that, he grabbed Zichun's sleeve:

[Can we go together? ]

Zichun stood up, and the people in the dining hall also stood up. Everyone seemed to be pushed by an invisible force, and unconsciously followed them out of the dining hall together.

After getting in the car, Bo Tang stretched out his head and said loudly:

[Please take care of things for me for now, Zhiguang; I will have a reply immediately after I see my father. Peiyu, you should make a phone call first······]

In less than half an hour, Zhiguang and Peiyu had received Bo Tang's letter, which meant:

[I have met with the old man, and everything is fundamentally safe now. There is no need to worry about anything. Notify the factory as soon as possible to hand over the supplies according to the agreement. The defense lines of both Yu are withdrawn at the same time. Someone should also be sent to notify Ma Wenqing. I will be back soon, and the rest will be discussed in person·····]

The atmosphere inside and outside this building immediately returned to normal; the words in the letter were also executed separately by Zhiguang and Peiyu. It was not until Bo Tang came back in the evening that everyone knew the origin of Yongsun Gan's wonderful trick: Later, Bo Tang recounted the process:

[They have been there for the eighth day today. It is said that Lao Wu can get more than a thousand yuan a day, and by the morning before yesterday, she had already gotten a very good amount. This is of course all thanks to the old man's face. Zichun felt that this kind of friendship—I'm embarrassed to say it's a favor—should be specially repaid, so the day before yesterday, they decided to take advantage of his thirty-third birthday today to become the old man's godson, and to become a publicly recognized and legitimate godson. The old man certainly had no objection, so they agreed on a date: later, they thought that Zichun was actually one or two years older than me, and it would seem awkward if he suddenly called me brother in the future, so they asked me to be there as well, which meant to ask me to recognize it. They had already set up incense, flowers, and candles in their house, and were preparing to kowtow formally at eight o'clock—that is, at Xu time—we have to hurry up and deliver the gifts·····Haha, isn't it funny! Speaking of gambling, they originally planned to gamble for another three or four days, and they were going to stop after the Lantern Festival, but of course there's no talking about it now······Haha·I heard that the big losers are two famous wastrels in Shanghai, one surnamed Zhou and one surnamed Cheng, and they each lost twenty or thirty thousand! ] Bo Tang said such a long passage with great animation, and then fiddled with his fur robe to tidy up the clothes inside, and continued after a while:

[Isn't it funny! As for me, I'm lucky that my luck is still good, and I'll only have to spend a few more dollars on Ma Wenqing's thank you gift in the future! ······The old man's matter is finally settled: Zhiguang, have we handed over the supplies to Zhabei clearly? ] The next morning, Zhiguang and Representative Qiu and a few others had already walked to Bo Tang's house, and calmly took out a receipt from the ××× Association.

│Written in Shanghai in July of the 22nd year│

Business Experience (31)

Dried Scallops Should Be Called Jiang Yaozhu 243

Zheng Xinsheng

Jiang Yao, also known as Yu Yu, is produced in the offshore waters. The shell is long and thin, making a right triangle. The surface has scales, arranged in a radial shape. The inside of the shell is black with a slight shimmer. The meat is not edible, but the two pillars before and after it are very delicious. Take it down and dry it in the sun, sell it for food, which is Jiang Yaozhu, commonly known as dried scallops.

Jiang Yaozhu is a must-have item for restaurants, and ordinary people often eat it, and it is often listed as a common dish, so the sales are quite wide, but Japanese goods are the majority. Domestic products include Yantai dried scallops, which are in good shape and the price is relatively cheap. Now it is described in detail, so that consumers can know how to identify when buying and using.

Yantai dried scallops, the color is tender yellow, but there is no bright light, the shape is like a short cylinder, the size is different, the taste is fresh and tender. Japanese goods have round grains, triangular two kinds, produced in Japan Hakone, Kitami, Aomori, etc., the difference between it and Yantai goods, in addition to the triangular dried scallops are irregular polygonal, the shape is obviously different, it can be known at a glance. Round dried scallops, the color is bright yellow, slightly bright, the silk pattern is more delicate, although the shape is the same as a cylinder, but if you look closely, the middle part of the Japanese goods is larger, and the upper and lower ends are slightly smaller, like the gongs and drums in the old medicine reputation, and the Yantai goods are neat up and down, without much difference. If the two types are compared at the same time, it is not difficult to distinguish. The current market price of Yantai goods is about 110 yuan, and Japanese goods increase by about 10% to 20%.

Jiang Yaozhu has many uses, and here is one of them. Half a tael of dried scallops, soaked in water, three fresh eggs, shelled and beaten thoroughly, put in the pot and stir-fry, add one or two scallions, lightly sprinkle yellow wine, add salty heads, and eat it when it is cooked. Its taste is rich, fat and delicious, and incomparable.

Advertising and Modern Commerce and Culture 244

— Wen

Sitting in a scorching small room, my chest feels strangely greasy and my mind is strangely hazy. I idly chatted with Mr. Wu about things that had nothing to do with me, and gradually we talked about the key to success in modern commerce. The first, of course, is to have strong capital, because modern commerce is absolutely a matter of [big frogs eating small frogs] and [cats catching mice]. Without large capital, one cannot independently form a [trust], and will inevitably not only fail to profit or monopolize, but will also lose money and collapse. The second is to rely on the blind, reckless hype of advertising, which confuses the consumer's innate decision-making power and makes them feel wholeheartedly convinced. As for things like so-called [speculation] and [established brands], these are minor details that are not of great importance. Take the several trust-like businesses in Shanghai: ×× candy store, ×× foreign goods company, ×× national medicine store, ×× tea store, all have many as a dozen branches, and at least three or five branches. Since the capital is strong, large-scale advertisements are frequently published in daily newspapers, so customers flock to them, naturally benefiting several times over and the business is very developed. The remaining small stores in the same industry are either closing their doors and renting out, or selling off their stock. But as for ×× calligraphy and painting supplies store, since the capital is strong (with countless branches), and the hype is deafening, it has declined like silk and satin companies and Chinese-style shoe stores. This is because of the decline of Chinese culture: fountain pens have replaced writing brushes, Western clothing has replaced Chinese clothing, and leather shoes have replaced cloth shoes. This is an exceptional, major issue of national importance, which cannot be fully discussed here.

Speaking of culture, advertising has become even more of a captive of culture. To put it more strongly, modern culture is almost advertising culture. Without the help of advertising, it would be as difficult to open a business as it is for a small store.

××'s White Turbidity Pills, although a family secret passed down for generations, are miraculously effective, but they still need to be advertised frequently in various newspapers in special fonts. Only in this way can patriotic compatriots, if they happen to suffer from white turbidity, pry open their money boxes and rush to buy ××'s White Turbidity Pills, one box to eradicate the root cause. Even if one box does not eradicate the root cause (obviously not as effective as advertised), they will comfort themselves: [It's probably because the disease has penetrated the bone marrow, and another box is needed.]

Before ××, a great physician, hangs up his medicine gourd, he always wants to persuade several important celebrities to publish an introductory advertisement first. The author once suffered from an illness in City C, and invited a doctor to see him. He refused the fee, only saying that he wanted me to publish an acknowledgment in the newspaper in the future. Unfortunately, he did not cure my illness, and I have not published the announcement to this day.

Just looking at these few examples of medicine and culture, one can know the great magic of advertising. (The medical and pharmaceutical industry is one of the broader cultures.)

And look, the era is the summer of 1933. In the education sector, schools are busy enrolling students, and in the publishing sector, elementary school textbooks are selling too much, and general publications and newspapers are booming. This is not only the situation since the [September 18th] [January 28th] incidents, but also the unprecedented excitement of the past three or four years.

It is necessary for schools to advertise for enrollment, but it is not necessary to brag so much in the advertisement. The chairman is a famous celebrity, the principal is a doctoral degree, the school scenery is how, the curriculum is how practical, the history is how long, etc., all of which are boasted up, the purpose is to confuse the eyes of the candidates. There are even those who publish their cheap advertisements in the educational news, so that it is not difficult to attract students.

When advertising textbooks, it is necessary to print the comments drawn from various parties, and it is necessary to print the titles of the reviewers │ │ what expert director and director of the education bureau. In fact, the so-called comments are all a few common phrases. It often happens that the same can be seen on the textbook advertisements of other companies, which is because some kind old gentlemen gave the comments to this company, and stuffed it into the pockets of the people who asked for it from that company, resulting in such a joke. There is nothing else, sales depend on advertising and publicity, and the fundamental way out lies in advertising.

When publishing publications and newspapers, it is necessary to invite celebrities to write inscriptions, famous painters to draw covers, and to specifically bring up the names of old writers for publicity. When reprinting, it is necessary to compile [rave reviews] [collection], forge readers' commendation letters, and blindly boast and praise themselves.

In short, culture must rely on advertising to sway people, which is the characteristic of culture at this stage, and it is also the inevitable distortion of culture at this stage.

Side Business of Rickshaw Pullers 246

— Mei Cang

Since the opening of the Beijing-Hangzhou National Highway, many passengers traveling between here have switched from trains and ships to cars. This Shanghai bus station is attached to the Nanbu Station, Songjiang, in the Minhang area of Shanghai. I, who was born and raised in Songjiang and work in Shanghai, took a long-distance bus to Shanghai with a friend on Monday morning last week. Once we arrived at our destination, rickshaw pullers swarmed to solicit business as usual. For the price of two dimes, one of them pulled us to Fourth Avenue. Two vehicles using people as horses were rushing forward. When I write to this point, I can only describe how the construction in the Chinese area is progressing and how the market is recovering after the war. It is not the whole story. When the car arrived at the Shanghai Local Court (formerly known as the Local Office before the establishment of the judicial authorities in the Chinese area), the two horse-powered rickshaw pullers suddenly stopped the car and said to me, "Sir, the sun is so hot, let me put up the canopy for you to shade you." As soon as he finished speaking, half of his body was pressed tightly against mine. I saw him holding up the canopy with one hand, and heard him shouting in his mouth; "Oh! The canopy is broken!" At the same time, I felt a rough, foreign force attacking my money clip at the edge of my short shirt pocket. Haha, although I have never passed three levels or opened a pier, I immediately recognized their mystery at that time, and immediately asked him in a warning tone what he was doing. Unexpectedly, there were many unexpected things. Not only did he not stop his behavior at that time, but he even used a strong grab-style move to try to get his object (money clip). At this time, I jumped out of the car and negotiated with him, and then cut off his idea. At the same time, my friend also encountered the same move, but the entry point of his article was named after teasing his long shirt, and the real thing was stealing. After two discussions, I realized that most of the rickshaw pullers in this section also have this job. If one person succeeds and the victim shouts, they come in groups to persuade them, and their doctrine is to let the successful rickshaw puller go, and pull this victim to Laoximen at a very low price, so their cars only have notifications from the Chinese area. The reason why they want to take business in the concession is only to do this trick and then pull you to the junction of the Chinese and foreign concessions, and call a car to the concession for you. As for when they start, the distance from the patrol police's post is very far, so even if you shout, it is difficult to hear.

This is the sign of [×× Layman's Fortune Telling Hall] that I see every day when I pass by, on both sides of the door; commenting on the noble creation of [a certain important person] and the noble character of [×× General], etc. In addition, there are portraits of important people of the era hanging, arranged in five colors without order.

Why is it that in this prosperous metropolis; not afraid that is where the government is located, Nanjing││there are also many doing such business in the Confucius Temple now. I think: In modern China, there are openly such people who have achieved victory on the front line of life, and are on par with the general rich and noble people who go in and out of big hotels and live in rooms that cost a dozen yuan a month. This shows that Chinese scholars (I call them Chinese scientists) are admired by the general "rich" and "important people," and they are truly worthy of being a famous "Divine State Ancient Country."

In the Children's Park 248

— Ms. Yan Yan

One day, I went to Hongkou Park with my seven-year-old younger sister.

The swings are the most cherished by children. Indeed, they are quite good. Swinging gently gives one a feeling of floating in the air. Moreover, the gentle summer breeze is so comfortable and pleasant!

There were already five or six children standing beside the swings. Because my younger sister arrived first, she was able to occupy a spot. She probably used it for twenty minutes. A Japanese woman with two children smiled and said to me in a very Shanghai-accented way:

"China Miss! Please ask your younger sister to stop for a moment, and let my little darling play for a while. I will return it to you later!"

I was neither for nor against it, but I was a little hesitant in my heart, because other Chinese children beside me had also made reservations with me. Now, several children wanted to play. I didn't know who to let go first.

Seeing that I had no expression, she said further:

"I came before them. This is a park!"

She said the word "park" very loudly, as if telling me to recognize that it was a park and that I should know the rules. Indeed, she came before them. According to reason, I should let her go first. However, the concept of the nation hovered in my mind. How could I not hesitate?

Finally, I asked my younger sister to give it to the Japanese woman. However, a reproachful voice immediately entered my ears: "Why did you give it to her? Why not give it to your own Chinese people? You are truly a complete slave of a fallen nation..."

I was scolded by them, and my heart was immediately confused. I regretted that I should not have given it to the Japanese, but I planned to argue with them. I didn't even know what to say. I only felt a little dizzy.

I could no longer stand in the park. I took my sister's hand and ran desperately out of the park, jumping onto a "Route 1" bus that was about to leave.

The wheels were shaking, and at the same time, my heart was still uneasy.

Shop Assistant Correspondence 250

Can't you work if you are deaf? Dear Editor:

I have a very difficult problem to solve. I have long wanted to write to you for advice, because I can't write well, and I'm afraid you won't like it. Now I am wandering all night and have no other way. So I have no choice but to write this letter to ask you for advice, hoping that you will not refuse my request. Please give me your honest guidance, like precious jade, to lead me out of my confusion! When I was nineteen years old (i.e., 1930), I worked as a junior clerk in a tobacco company. But unfortunately, I didn't serve for half a year before I had a serious illness that brought me back from the dead. Later, I finally recovered, but my ears were deafened by the illness. The ringing in my ears was so loud and painful. I was inexplicably frustrated and disheartened. When the company stopped my business, there was no reason to argue, so I had to go back to eat my hometown rice.

Time flies, and three years have passed in a hurry. During these three years, I have consulted many famous doctors. But none of them have worked, and I have spent a lot of money. Inevitably, it added a lot of economic pressure, the family's fortunes declined, and disputes and ridicule often arose, which were unbearable. As a last resort, I finally came to rely on my relatives for recommendations in March of this year, but so far, all my plans have failed. Maybe it's because I'm old and deaf? I think you, sir, have seen and heard a lot, so you must be able to explain this problem for me. I don't know if there are any specialist doctors for the elderly and deaf in Shanghai. Please introduce me! If I can escape this sea of suffering, I will be grateful. If it has become an incurable disease, then I want to ask you for the second step. What can the deaf do to serve? Or what kind of industry can I learn in a short time? If there is no one who can do it, then there is no place for me in this society? This is my last and only hope. Please give me a gospel. Sincerely yours, Ren Zhensheng

× × × × ×

Editor's Note: The causes of deafness can generally be divided into two types: The first is the deformity, incompleteness, obstruction, or damage of the auditory organs. Except for a few very simple symptoms, most of this type of deafness is untreatable. Although someone has recently invented a very sophisticated hearing aid, claiming that those who use it can turn deafness into hearing, it is still in the experimental stage and cannot be widely adopted. The second is the weakness of the constitution, which affects the auditory nerves, resulting in complete hearing loss. Most of this type of deafness has the hope of being cured. Because if we use medicine to gradually strengthen the constitution, the auditory nerves will naturally become gradually active.

Whether Mr. Ren's deafness can be cured, it is best to consult a competent Western doctor for diagnosis. According to what we know, there is a German doctor named Aks across from the Youth Association on Sichuan Road in this city. He is very confident in ophthalmology, otolaryngology, and stomatology. You can ask him to diagnose you and ask him if he has any hope of curing you.

If the result of the diagnosis is unfortunately [incurable], then don't be discouraged and say such absolute things as [there is no place for me in the world]. You must know that there are many things in the world that deaf people can do. Moreover, there are several things that [must be done by the deaf]! As for writing them down item by item, it is not possible within the space here, and there are questions about whether you can find what you want and whether you can be competent. So I am publishing your letter publicly here, hoping that a kind hand will reach out from this vast society to help you!

Under the Traffic Lights (53) 251

— Xi Lin

(28) The Third Mistress greedily looked at his departing figure without answering.

"Ah, Brother Qiao, are you angry with me?"

Still no answer.

"Won't you forgive me?" | "Fortunately... Wang Hua has been kidnapped now!" Shi Qiao wanted to ask for clarification, but didn't.

"He was kidnapped last night, led by that Long Fa. They say it's not just kidnapping for money, his life is probably in danger! Can you find a way to save Jiefu? Only Jiefu and Wang Hua were kidnapped!"

Shi Qiao understood most of it. He was about to leave to call for a rickshaw. The Third Mistress approached him pleadingly, trying to grab his hand:

"I heard last night that Wang Hua said you were coming back in the next few days, so I was going to rush back to see you. Unfortunately, this happened, making me anxious for half the night with no news at all. It's all Jiefu's fault. Last night at Zhao Yishan's house, when they heard firecrackers, some advocated still watching the fun, while others said that maybe the war situation had changed and the discussion of the free market could be slowed down, and that this kind of thing was not guaranteed to work anyway. It was him and Wu Ziqing who insisted on continuing. Well, Long Fa led a dozen people with guns to rush in." Shi Qiao heard everything and secretly felt happy, but he didn't show any expression on his face, which made the Third Mistress unable to be coquettish or seductive. Fortunately, it wasn't quite dawn yet, and she was still able to grab Shi Qiao's hand in the dim light, not afraid of the rickshaw pullers peeking:

"Brother Qiao, forgive me, let's talk in the room!" | "Brother Qiao, from now on, I'll only listen to you, I'm only yours."

But Shi Qiao didn't want to. As if he had been stung by a needle, he fiercely shook off her hand and went forward to shout for a rickshaw.

The car stopped in front of the house a little further away, and the Third Mistress had no choice but to go upstairs in disappointment. It was good to see Shi Qiao's at the door, pretending not to be in the room, and walking to the balcony to look downstairs, pouting, but no one came to buy her account.
